in rebuttal, and to conduct such cross examination as may be required for a
full and complete disclosure of facts.
   H.   The hearing officer may limit expert opinion evidence in his/her
discretion.
   I.   Rules of privilege recognized by law shall be applicable.
   J.   After first advising of intention to do so, notice may be taken of
judicially cognizable facts as is provided by law.
   K.   Documentary evidence may be received in the form of copies or excerpts
or by incorporation by reference.
   L.   The provisions of ORS 183.450 shall be applicable. (Ord. 157, 6-14-
2006)
3-1-8: PROPOSED ORDERS IN CONTESTED CASES; EXCEPTIONS AND ARGUMENTS:
   A.   If a majority of officials from the county court who are to render a
final order are not present at a hearing or have not reviewed and considered
the record, and the order is adverse to a party (excluding the county), a
proposed order, including findings of fact and conclusions of law, shall be
served upon the parties.
   B.   The parties shall be given the opportunity to file exceptions and
present arguments to the officials who render the final order.
   C.   The hearing officer shall prepare and serve on the county and all
parties to hearing a proposed order, including recommended findings of fact and
conclusions of law. The proposed order shall become final after the twentieth
day following the date of service of the proposed order, unless the county
within that period issues an amended order. (Ord. 157, 6-14-2006)
3-1-9: FINAL ORDERS IN CONTESTED CASES; NOTIFICATION:
   A.   Final orders in contested cases shall be in writing and include the
following:
      1.   Rulings: Rulings on admissibility of offered evidence;
      2.   Findings Of Fact: Those matters which are either agreed as fact or
which, when disputed, are determined by the fact finder, on substantial
evidence, to be a fact over contentions to the contrary;
      3.   Conclusions Of Law: Applications of the controlling law to the facts
found at the legal results arising therefrom; and
      4.   Order: The action taken by the county as a result of the findings of
fact and conclusions of law.
   B.   Parties to contested cases and their attorneys on record shall be
served a copy of the final order by mail. Parties shall be notified of their
right to a judicial review of the order including the cite to ORS 183.484.
(Ord. 157, 6-14-2006)
3-1-10: RECONSIDERATION; REHEARING:
   A.   A party may file a petition for reconsideration or rehearing on a final
order with the county within thirty (30) days after the order is served.
   B.   The petition shall set forth the specific grounds for requesting the
reconsideration or rehearing. The petition may be supported by a written
argument.
   C.   The county may grant a reconsideration petition if sufficient reason is
made to appear. If the petition is granted, an amended order shall be entered.
   D.   The county may grant a rehearing if sufficient reason therefor is made
to appear. The rehearing may be limited by the county to specific matters.
   E.   If the county does not act on the petition within sixty (60) days
following the date the petition was filed, the petition shall be deemed denied.
   F.   A petition for rehearing or reconsideration need not be filed as
condition of judicial review. (Ord. 157, 6-14-2006)
3-1-11: CIVIL PENALTIES:
   A.   Civil penalties may be levied in the manner provided by ORS 183.745 and
OAR 333-157-0045.
   B.   A civil penalty imposed under this section shall become due and payable
ten (10) days after the order imposing the civil penalty becomes final by
operation of law or on appeal. A person against whom a civil penalty is to be
imposed shall be served with a notice in the form and manner provided by
section
3-1-3 of this chapter.
   C.   Any person who requests a hearing within the time allowed shall be
entitled to a hearing. The hearing shall be conducted pursuant to section
3-1-6 of this chapter. If a hearing is not requested within the time allowed, a
final order imposing the civil penalty shall be made. (Ord. 157, 6-14-2006)
3-1-12: REVIEW:
The provisions of ORS chapter 183, otherwise applicable to contested case
proceedings and civil penalties shall apply. (Ord. 157, 6-14-2006)
CHAPTER 2
OUTDOOR MASS GATHERINGS
SECTION:
3-2-1:   Statutes And Rules Incorporated
3-2-2:   Definitions
3-2-3:   Permit Required
3-2-4:   Application
3-2-5:   Fee
3-2-6:   Permit Process For Outdoor Mass Gatherings When Gathering Does Not
Require A Land Use Permit
3-2-7:   Waiver
3-2-8:   Insurance
3-2-9:   Administrator
3-2-10:   Sheriff
3-2-11:   Fire And Emergency Medical Services
3-2-12:   Health Officer And Environmental Health Officer
3-2-13:   Temporary Permit May Be Required
3-2-14:   Other Types Of Assemblies Distinguished
3-2-15:   Enforcement
3-2-1: STATUTES AND RULES INCORPORATED:
   ORS 433.735 to 433.770 and 433.990(6) (the statutes) and OAR 333-039-0005 to
333-039-0055 (the administrative rules) which regulate mass gatherings, are
incorporated herein by this reference and apply to outdoor mass gatherings as
defined by this chapter. However, where this chapter provides a standard,
procedure or definition different than the statutes and/or rules, this chapter
shall control. (Ord. 189, 11-3-2010)
3-2-2: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter:
   COUNTY COURT: The county court for Malheur County, Oregon.
   ORGANIZER: Includes any person who holds, stages or sponsors an outdoor mass
gathering and the owner, lessee or possessor of the real property upon which
the outdoor mass gathering is to take place.
   OUTDOOR MASS GATHERING: An actual or reasonably anticipated assembly of 750
or more persons at any time on land within the unincorporated areas of Malheur
County which continues and can reasonably be expected to continue for more than
five (5) hours but not more than 120 hours within any three-month period, which
is held primarily in open spaces and not in any permanent structure. Included
are hours necessary to set up the gathering or clean up afterward. Excluded are
hours required for ingress to egress from a gathering that is located on lands
zoned Exclusive Farm Use that are 60 miles or farther from the nearest
interstate highway.
   PERMANENT STRUCTURE: Includes a stadium, an arena, an auditorium, a
coliseum, a fairground or other similar established places for assemblies.
   TEMPORARY STRUCTURE: Includes tents, trailers, chemical toilet facilities
and other structures customarily erected or sited for temporary use. (Ord. 189,
11-3-2010; amd. Ord. 225, 10-14-2020)
3-2-3: PERMIT REQUIRED:
   A.   No organizer shall hold, conduct, advertise or otherwise promote an
outdoor mass gathering or allow an outdoor mass gathering to be held on real
property the organizer owns, leases or possesses unless a permit to hold such
outdoor mass gathering has been issued by the county court.
   B.   A permit issued under this chapter does not entitle the organizer to
make any permanent physical alterations to or on real property. (Ord. 189, 11-
3-2010)
3-2-4: APPLICATION:
An application, more than sixty (60) days prior to the first day of the
gathering, shall be submitted by the organizer to the county court. The
application shall include:
   A.   Names, addresses, date of birth and telephone number of all persons
organizing, promoting and sponsoring the outdoor mass gathering.
   B.   Dates, number of days, hours of the days and total duration of the
outdoor mass gathering, including set up and clean up.
   C.   The location or site of the outdoor mass gathering, including site
dimensions. Include legal description, address and zoning designation of site.
   D.   Plans for sanitation, fire protection, medical services, public safety,
security, parking, traffic flow and public roads to be accessed.
   E.   The number of persons anticipated to attend the outdoor mass gathering
at any one time, and the number of persons expected to attend the entire event.
Organizer must be able to keep a reasonable count of persons and vehicles
entering and leaving the outdoor mass gathering and, if necessary, to limit
admissions to comply with attendance numbers estimated by organizer.
   F.   Nature of proposed gathering. Food being served and by whom, cost to
attend, whether sound amplification will be used, a statement whether alcohol
will be made available etc.
   G.   Signed certification of the accuracy and truthfulness of the statements
made in the application.
   H.   Incomplete applications will not be processed. (Ord. 189, 11-3-2010)
3-2-5: FEE:
Before accepting an application for an outdoor mass gathering permit, the
county court shall collect an application fee. The fee shall be set, and may be
changed, by order or resolution of the county court. In setting or changing the
fee, the county court will consider the reasonable and necessary costs incurred
by the sheriff, fire agency, county health and environmental health officers,
road supervisor and other agencies and officials, in reviewing and processing
the application, inspecting the assembly site and ensuring the safety of
persons and property at, and in the vicinity of, the outdoor mass gathering.
The fee shall not exceed five thousand dollars ($5,000.00), unless the limit in
ORS 433.750(6) is increased. (Ord. 189, 11-3-2010; amd. Ord. 225, 10-14-2020)
3-2-6: PERMIT PROCESS FOR OUTDOOR MASS GATHERINGS WHEN GATHERING DOES NOT
REQUIRE A LAND USE PERMIT:
Upon receipt of an application and permit fee to hold an outdoor mass
gathering, the county court shall give notice of the application to the county
sheriff, the fire district, ambulance district and ambulance provider in which
the outdoor mass gathering is to be held, the county environmental and public
health officers and the county road supervisor. The county court may, in
addition, request comment on the application from any other agency or official
who may be affected by the application. The county court shall publish and post
notice, and hold a public hearing on the application in the manner required by
ORS 433.750. After holding the hearing and considering the evidence and
testimony submitted, the county court shall determine whether to issue the
permit. In any case, the county court shall not grant a permit for an outdoor
mass gathering unless the organizer can:
   A.   Demonstrate compliance with or the ability to comply with the
administrative rules and conditions of permit.
   B.   Demonstrate that the proposed outdoor mass gathering will not make any
permanent physical alterations to or on the real property, which is the site of
the outdoor mass gathering, or materially alter the capability to use the real
property upon which the outdoor mass gathering is to be held in the future for
uses designated under the real property's comprehensive plan and zoning
designation.
   C.   Demonstrate compliance with or the ability to comply with the
requirements of the Oregon liquor control commission (OLCC), if alcohol is
served.
   D.   Demonstrate that the proposed outdoor mass gathering will not
unreasonably disturb persons or property in the vicinity of the gathering for
reasons such as, but not limited to, excessive noise or dust. When sound
amplification is used, no outdoor mass gathering shall be conducted within one
thousand feet (1,000') of any neighboring residence between the hours of eleven
o'clock (11:00) P.M. and nine o'clock (9:00) A.M. The county court, in its
discretion, may impose other noise restrictions and specify a noise control
level if the county court determines that doing so is necessary to preserve the
comfort and repose of neighboring residents.
   E.   Consent, in writing, to allow law enforcement, public and environmental
health and fire control officers to come upon the premises for which the permit
has been granted for the purpose of inspection and enforcement of the terms and
conditions of the permit issued. If deficiencies are not cured or cannot be
cured, a county code enforcement officer may revoke the outdoor mass gathering
permit. If the organizer fails to remove all debris, structures and residue
from the site or adjacent property by the end of the one hundred twenty (120)
hours permitted for the event, a county code enforcement officer may issue a
public nuisance citation. In addition, the county may seek other and additional
remedies as set out in ORS 433.755(2).
   F.   Acknowledge that issuance of a permit by the county court pursuant to
this section shall not authorize an outdoor mass gathering unless the organizer
also secures the written statement of the county sheriff, as required by OAR
333-039-0050, and the written approval of the chief of the fire district in
which the gathering is to be held, or other local fire protection agency with
jurisdiction, as required by OAR 333-039-0045. (Ord. 189, 11-3-2010; amd. Ord.
225, 10-14-2020)
3-2-7: WAIVER:
An organizer of an outdoor mass gathering of less than one thousand (1,000)
persons may request a waiver from the county court regarding the requirement of
published notice and a hearing. The county court, in its discretion, may waive
the requirement of published notice and hearing if the organizer demonstrates
to the county court's satisfaction that the outdoor mass gathering will involve
less than one thousand (1,000) persons, that adjacent and nearby residents and
property owners have been notified of the outdoor mass gathering, and any
concerns of adjacent and nearby residents and property owners have been
addressed or will be addressed, and that the waiver is justified under the
circumstances. (Ord. 189, 11-3-2010)
3-2-8: INSURANCE:
The county court determines that outdoor mass gatherings inherently create a
potential for injury to persons and property. Therefore, organizers are
required to obtain an insurance policy in an amount not exceeding one million
dollars ($1,000,000.00). The policy of casualty insurance shall provide
coverage against liability for death, injury or disability of any human or for
damage to property arising out of the outdoor mass gathering. The county, its
officers, agents and employees, the sheriff, and the county health officer
shall be named as additional insureds under the policy. (Ord. 189, 11-3-2010)
3-2-9: ADMINISTRATOR:
The county court, by order or resolution, may appoint a person or position to
administer this chapter and applications filed pursuant to this chapter. (Ord.
189, 11-3-2010)
3-2-10: SHERIFF:
Upon receipt of an application for an outdoor mass gathering permit, the
sheriff shall consider the requirements of OAR 333-039-0050, security
personnel. (Ord. 189, 11-3-2010)
3-2-11: FIRE AND EMERGENCY MEDICAL SERVICES:
Upon receipt of an application for an outdoor mass gathering permit, the fire
district or agency, ambulance service district, ambulance service provider and
road supervisor shall consider the requirements of OAR 333-039-0040, emergency
medical facilities; OAR 333-039-0045, fire protection; and OAR 333-039-0055
traffic. (Ord. 189, 11-3-2010)
3-2-12: HEALTH OFFICER AND ENVIRONMENTAL HEALTH OFFICER:
Along with the notice of an application for an outdoor mass gathering permit,
the county court shall request the county health officer and environmental
health officer to recommend whether to approve or deny the permit considering
the requirements of OAR 333-039-0015, water supply; OAR 333-039-0020, drainage;
OAR 333-039-0025, sewerage facilities; OAR 333-039-0030, refuse storage and
disposal; and OAR 333-039-0035, food and sanitary food service. (Ord. 189, 11-
3-2010)
3-2-13: TEMPORARY PERMIT MAY BE REQUIRED:
No more than one permit may be issued under this chapter for an outdoor mass
gathering during any three (3) month period for the same organizer or property,
unless the organizer or landowner also applies for and receives a temporary or
conditional use permit pursuant to Malheur County zoning ordinance. (Ord. 189,
11-3-2010)
3-2-14: OTHER TYPES OF ASSEMBLIES DISTINGUISHED:
   A.   An actual or reasonably anticipated assembly of less than seven hundred
fifty (750) persons is not an outdoor mass gathering and is not a land use.
   B.   An actual or reasonably anticipated assembly of seven hundred fifty
(750) or more persons on land which does not constitute and is not reasonably
expected to continue for more than five (5) consecutive hours is not an outdoor
mass gathering and is not a land use.
   C.   Land Use Permit. An actual or reasonably anticipated assembly of more
than 3000 persons which continues or can reasonably be expected to continue for
more than 24 consecutive hours but less than 120 hours within any three-month
period and which is primarily in open spaces and not in a permanent structure
requires a land use permit (i.e. conditional use permit in the EFU zone). In
addition, the organizer must demonstrate compliance or that it can comply with
the requirements of this ordinance; and the requirements set out in ORS 433.750
and 433.755. An outdoor mass gathering requiring a land use permit must be
compatible with the existing land uses and cannot materially alter the
stability of the overall land use pattern of the area. The conduct of hearings,
notice provisions and approval criteria for a land use permit are set in ORS
433.763, ORS 215.402 to 215.438, the Malheur County Code and other applicable
state laws and administrative rules. A separate or additional fee may be
established by the planning department for a land use permit for outdoor mass
gatherings. (Ord. 189, 11-3-2010; amd. Ord. 225, 10-14-2020)
3-2-15: ENFORCEMENT:
This chapter may be enforced as provided by, and violators hereof are subject
to the penalties provided in, the Malheur County general enforcement
provisions, in addition to other remedies and penalties provided by statutes,
administrative rules and common law. (Ord. 189, 11-3-2010)
CHAPTER 3
NOXIOUS WEED CONTROL
SECTION:
3-3-1:   Title
3-3-2:   Purpose
3-3-3:   Definitions
3-3-4:   Weed Control District
3-3-5:   Weed Inspector
3-3-6:   List Of Noxious Weeds
3-3-7:   Notice
3-3-8:   Duties Of Owner
3-3-9:   Duty To Clean Machinery Before Moving; Weed Infested Residue Not To Be
Moved
3-3-10:   Eradication Of Noxious Weeds When Owner Refuses
3-3-11:   Expenses As Lien
3-3-12:   Penalties
3-3-13:   Other Remedies
3-3-14:   Jurisdiction
3-3-1: TITLE:
This chapter shall be known as the MALHEUR COUNTY WEED ORDINANCE. (Ord. 172,
12-5-2007)
3-3-2: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to specify the procedures for the control of
weeds identified as noxious by the Malheur County court and for areas within
the Malheur County Weed Control District. (Ord. 172, 12-5-2007; amd. Ord. 231,
4- 12-2023)
3-3-3: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following words shall have the following
meanings:
 
COUNTY COURT: The Malheur County court
              The Malheur County weed control district, the boundaries of which
DISTRICT:     coincide with the boundaries of Malheur County. Boundaries of
              incorporated cities are specifically excluded from the District.
 
 
              Real property within Malheur County outside the limits of a city
LAND:         upon which a violation of this chapter has occurred or is
              occurring.
              Any plant determined by the county court and recommended by the
NOXIOUS WEED: Weed Inspector to be injurious to public health, crops,
              livestock, land, or other property.
OWNER:        Any legal owner or any person having charge, care or control of
              land. (Ord. 172, 12-5-2007; amd. Ord. 231, 4-12-2023)
 
3-3-4: WEED CONTROL DISTRICT:
All of Malheur County outside the limits of any city is the weed control
district for the purpose of destroying and preventing the seeding and spread of
noxious weeds. The district is known as the Malheur County weed control
district. (Ord. 172, 12-5-2007)
3-3-5: WEED INSPECTOR:
The county court shall appoint a weed inspector, whose duties shall include,
but not be limited to, the following:
   A.   To discover whether any noxious weeds or plants are being permitted to
grow and produce bloom or seed within the district contrary to this chapter or
ORS 569.360 to ORS 569.495;
   B.   To serve notices;
   C.   When necessary, to destroy or cut, or to supervise the destruction or
cutting of noxious weeds growing or seeding within the district; and
   D.   To conduct investigations, approve plans, make expenditures within the
weed department budget and issue citations for violations of this chapter.
The weed inspector shall exercise discretion in fulfilling duties pursuant to
this chapter, consistent with the availability of funds and other resources.
(Ord. 172, 12-5-2007; amd. Ord. 231, 4-12-2023)
3-3-6: LIST OF NOXIOUS WEEDS:
For purposes of this chapter, weeds shall be declared noxious by their
inclusion on a list adopted by resolution of the county court, upon the
recommendation of the weed inspector. A weed may be added to, re-prioritized or
deleted from the list of noxious weeds by resolution of the county court.
Noxious weeds shall be designated and control prioritized into A, B and C
groups. Priorities may be adjusted within the county at the discretion of the
weed inspector with permission of the county court. (Ord. 172, 12-5-2007)
3-3-7: NOTICE:
   A.   When it appears that violation of ORS chapter 569 or this chapter has
occurred, the weed inspector shall serve a written notice to the owner of the
land. If the weed inspector is unable to serve the notice personally, the weed
inspector shall post the notice and two (2) copies thereof in three (3)
conspicuous places on the land. If notice is posted, the weed inspector shall
also mail a copy of the notice to the owner or occupant of the land by both
regular mail and certified mail, return receipt requested.
   B.   The notice shall contain at least the following:
      1.   The date of service or posting of the notice;
      2.   The name of the noxious weed or weeds growing on the land; and
      3.   A statement setting forth that the noxious weeds must be destroyed
or must be prevented from producing seed within a specified period of time,
which shall be within the discretion of the weed inspector, but in no event
shall be less than two (2) days or more than twenty (20) days from the date of
service or posting.
   C.   A copy of the notice, together with proof of service or posting
endorsed thereon, shall be filed with the county court.
   D.   Notwithstanding the above, with permission of the landowner or
occupant, employees of the State Department of Agriculture, or agents of the
weed control district or weed inspector, may enter the land to identify noxious
weeds and to implement or provide for the implementation of integrated noxious
weed control measures, including but not limited to the application of
pesticides to the land. The control or eradication of noxious weeds may be
conducted with or without charge to the owner or occupant of the land. A notice
described in subsection B. above is not required for the conduct of activities
described in this subsection. (Ord. 172, 12-5-2007; amd. Ord. 231, 4-12-2023)
3-3-8: DUTIES OF OWNER:
   A.   Upon service or posting of the notice provided in section
3-3-7  of this chapter, any owner of the land shall destroy the noxious weed or
weeds specified in the notice or prevent the noxious weed or weeds from seeding
or spreading.
   B.   Every owner shall destroy or prevent the seeding on the owner's land of
any weed classified as a noxious weed by the county court using the most
efficient and practical means available and within the time declared reasonable
by the weed inspector. In no event shall a noxious weed be permitted to produce
seed. The means used to destroy or prevent the seeding of noxious weeds shall
comply with all applicable laws and label instructions. (Ord. 172, 12-5-2007;
amd. Ord. 231, 4- 12-2023)
3-3-9: DUTY TO CLEAN MACHINERY BEFORE MOVING; WEED INFESTED RESIDUE NOT TO BE
MOVED:
   A.   No person operating or having control of any threshing machinery,
clover huller, hay baler, seed cleaning or treating machinery or other
machinery shall move said machinery over any public road or from one farm to
another without first being thoroughly swept and cleaned.
   B.   All hay, straw or other crop residue infested with noxious weeds having
partially or fully formed seeds shall not be moved from the land on which grown
to other lands not infested with any of the weeds in the field from which such
crop material came. (Ord. 231, 4-12-2023)
3-3-10: ERADICATION OF NOXIOUS WEEDS WHEN OWNER REFUSES:
   A.   In the event that any owner or occupant of land fails or refuses to
destroy or cut noxious weeds within the time period specified in the notice
provided in section
3-3-7  of this chapter; or a person fails to comply with section
3-3-9  of this chapter, the weed inspector may issue a citation to the owner,
and/or seek injunctive relief in the Malheur County justice court to force
compliance with this chapter.
   B.   In addition, the weed inspector may go upon the land of the owner and
destroy or cut the noxious weeds or control them in a manner that will destroy
all seeds of such noxious weeds. The weed inspector and persons authorized by
the weed inspector may enter upon the property to abate the weed violation only
upon obtaining consent of the owner or a court issued warrant or upon obtaining
authority from the county court.
   C.   In the event destruction or control of the noxious weeds on any farm is
in the judgment of the weed inspector impracticable because the weeds are too
far advanced, or if for any other reason the means of control available are
unsatisfactory, the weed inspector shall notify the county court, who may
request the state department of agriculture to immediately quarantine the
noxious weed infested farm within the county to prevent the movement of
infested crops or livestock from the farm except under conditions prescribed in
the quarantine that will prevent the spread of noxious weeds by such crops or
livestock.
   D.   In all cases where the weed inspector undertakes to destroy or control
noxious weeds, the most effective and practical method that will not cause
injury to the land or crops in the judgment of the weed inspector shall be
used.
   E.   Upon completion of the weed abatement process and such work as
specified herein by the weed inspector or other person so appointed and
authorized by the county court, the weed inspector or such other person shall
file with the county court and county clerk an itemized statement of the
expenses necessarily incurred in the destruction of the noxious weeds,
including the wages of the inspector, assistants, if any, or such other person,
verified by the oath of the weed inspector or person. (Ord. 172, 12-5-2007;
amd. Ord. 231, 4-12-2023)
3-3-11: EXPENSES AS LIEN:
   A.   When the statement of expenses is filed with the county court as
specified in section
3-3-10  of this chapter, the county clerk shall cause it to be entered upon a
lien docket prepared for that purpose. The amount of the charges and expenses
when so docketed shall constitute a first lien upon the owner's land or
premises, except as to taxes.
   B.   If the charges and expenses are not paid and the lien discharged by the
owner or occupant of such lands within ninety (90) days from the date the lien
is docketed, the county may recover the expenses in an action at law.
   C.   If within ten (10) days from the date of filing and docketing the lien
as provided herein or ORS 569.400 and 569.410, no objection have been filed
thereto, the county court shall pay to the person(s) so appointed by the court
to perform the work, out of the general funds or the county, the amount of such
lien. (Ord. 172, 12-5-2007; amd, Ord. 231, 4-12-2023)
3-3-12: PENALTIES:
   A.   Any person who violates sections
3-3-9  and
3-3-10  of this chapter shall be subject to a fine of not more than seven
hundred twenty dollars ($720.00) for a noncontinuing offense and a fine of not
more than one thousand dollars ($1,000.00) for a continuing offense.
   B.   Each day that this chapter is violated shall constitute a separate
violation. (Ord. 172, 12-5-2007; amd. Ord. 231, 4-12-2023)
3-3-13: OTHER REMEDIES:
The provisions of this chapter are in addition to and not in lieu of any other
procedures and remedies provided by law including equitable relief and damages.
(Ord. 172, 12-5-2007; amd. Ord. 231, 4-12-2023)
3-3-14: JURISDICTION:
Jurisdiction for actions brought under this chapter shall be with the Malheur
County justice court for penalties as set out in
3-3-12 . All other matters in this chapter shall be heard before the county
court. (Ord. 172, 12-5-2007; amd. Ord. 231, 4-12-2023)
CHAPTER 4
PUBLIC NUISANCES
SECTION:
3-4-1:   Title
3-4-2:   Purpose
3-4-3:   Definitions
3-4-4:   General Prohibitions
3-4-5:   Notice Of Abatement
3-4-6:   Enforcement
3-4-1: TITLE:
This chapter shall be known as the MALHEUR COUNTY PUBLIC NUISANCE ORDINANCE.
(Ord. 183, 10-7-2009)
3-4-2: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to protect the health, safety and general
welfare of the people of Malheur County and protect the beauty of its
landscape. (Ord. 183, 10-7-2009)
3-4-3: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions apply:
   ABATE: To decrease in amount, clean up, eradicate, destroy and rectify the
problem.
   ACCUMULATION: Place, collect, pile, store, or keep on property.
   BUILDING: Any structure, mobile home or manufactured home.
      Abandoned Building: A building in which no one claims a right or interest
in or one that the owner has withdrawn all rights or interests in.
      Dangerous Building: A building that is deemed dangerous or unsafe when
any and or all of the conditions or defects that exist are to the extent that
the life, health, property or safety of the public or its occupants are
endangered. The county building official or the state fire marshal will make
the determination based on the Oregon building codes or Malheur County building
code.
      Vacant Building: A building unoccupied or unused for its intended purpose
for a period of twelve (12) consecutive months or longer shall be deemed
vacant. The unfinished exterior construction of a building when a building
permit has expired.
   HAZARDOUS APPLIANCE OR CONTAINER: Household appliances such as washers,
dryers, icebox, refrigerators, dishwashers, water heaters, stoves, and other
containers which are not being used for their intended purpose in their current
condition or which have an airtight lock or hook which may not be released from
inside and are being stored outside for more than a period of fourteen (14)
days.
   HOBBYIST OR OWNER: Vehicles or vehicle parts that are collected, purchased,
acquired, traded, restored, stored or maintained for the person's own use. This
shall include cars used in competition or racing. This shall include all
vehicles whether they are operable or inoperable.
   NUISANCE: For the purpose of this chapter, any act, omission, thing or
condition that, under the circumstances, causes injury, damage, annoyance,
inconvenience, discomfort, an offensive odor, is unsightly or degrades the
appearance of the area; is capable of causing an unreasonable threat of fire or
detriment to public health, safety and welfare; interferes with another's use
and enjoyment of real property; or interferes with the substantial and
unreasonable invasion of a right common to members of the general public.
   NUISANCE TREE, PLANT OR VEGETATION: Any plant, grass or tree (alive or dead)
causing or capable of causing an unreasonable threat to public health, safety
and welfare including, but not limited to: a tree, plant or vegetation
attractive to climb; a tree, plant or vegetation that may damage property and
utilities by falling due to its condition or size, overhang or height; or a
tree, plant or vegetation that blocks the vision of pedestrian or vehicular
traffic. This definition includes poison oak, hazardous thickets, noxious weeds
and dangerous vegetation that is a health or fire hazard. This definition does
not include agricultural crops.
   OFFENSIVE LITTERING: Consistent with ORS 164.805, a person commits the
violation of offensive littering if the person creates an objectionable stench
or degrades the beauty or appearance of property or detracts from the natural
cleanliness or safety of property by intentionally: discarding or depositing
any rubbish, trash, garbage, debris or other refuse or solid waste upon the
land of another without permission of the owners, or upon any public way or in
or upon any public transportation facility. Draining or causing or permitting
to be drained, garbage, debris or other refuse or solid waste upon a public way
or in or upon any public transportation facility. Permitting any rubbish,
trash, garbage, debris or other refuse or solid waste to be thrown from a
vehicle, which the person is operating. This definition does not apply to a
person operating a vehicle transporting passengers for hire subject to
regulation by interstate of commerce commission of the public utility
commission of Oregon, or to a person operating a school bus described in ORS
801.460.
   OWNER/RESPONSIBLE PERSON: Any legal owner or person having charge, care or
control of property or premises such as a contract purchaser, lessee, occupant,
agent or tenant.
   PERSONS: Individuals, corporations, associations, firms, partnerships,
government (local, federal or state), trust, estate, joint stock companies or
any other legal entity.
   PROPERTY: A developed or undeveloped lot or parcel and all improvements
located thereon as located within Malheur County.
   UNFIT FOR USE: A determination made by the Oregon health division that means
the property or building has been found to be, or there are reasonable grounds
to believe that the building or property was the site of illegal drug
manufacturing.
   VEHICLES: Any motor vehicle or motor vehicle parts. This includes, but is
not limited to, vehicles that are wrecked, dismantled, scrapped, ruined, used,
untitled, operable, inoperable, domestic, agricultural, commercial, industrial,
hobby or collectibles.
   WASTE: Useless, unwanted or discarded material. The fact that materials,
which would otherwise come within the definition of waste, may from time to
time have value, and thus be utilized or wanted shall not be removed from this
definition. Waste includes solid waste, hazardous solid waste and putrescible
waste.
      Hazardous Solid Waste: Solid waste, which may, by itself or in
combination with other solid waste or naturally occurring substances, be
infectious, poisonous, caustic, toxic, otherwise dangerous or injurious to
humans, plants, or animals.
      Putrescible Waste: Solid waste or sludge containing organic material that
can be rapidly decomposed by microorganisms, which may give rise to foul
smelling, offensive products such as animal carcasses that attract or provide
food for birds, animals, and insects including potential disease vectors such
as rats or rodents.
      Solid Waste: Shall include all putrescible and nonputrescible waste,
including, but not limited to, garbage, rubbish, refuse, ashes, junk,
wastepaper and cardboard, rubber products, petroleum products, plastics,
bottles, glass, cans and manmade products; grass clippings; compost; sewer
sludge; septic tank and cesspool pumpings; hazardous solid waste; hazardous
appliances and containers; residential, commercial, industrial, construction
and demolition waste; equipment and furniture; pieces of metal; inoperable
vehicles; vehicle parts and bodies; used motor oil, batteries, vehicle tires;
manure, vegetable, dead animals; and animal solid and semisolid waste. (Ord.
183, 10-7-2009)
3-4-4: GENERAL PROHIBITIONS:
No person shall cause or permit a nuisance on property that is owned or
controlled by the person. Nuisance includes:
   A.   Accumulations, deposits, dumping or disposal of solid waste or waste,
except:
      1.   Materials located in a duly licensed and authorized landfill or
waste disposal site licensed and maintained in accordance with local and state
law.
      2.   Materials accumulated for collection within seven (7) days by a
solid waste disposal service.
      3.   Materials in reasonable amounts to be used for fertilizer in an
agricultural operation or domestic garden. What is reasonable will be
determined by the size of the agricultural operation or domestic garden, zoning
of the property and proximity to residential and commercial structures.
      4.   Personal recycling completely enclosed and not visible from a public
road or to be disposed of within ninety (90) days.
   B.   Stagnant water that affords a breeding place for mosquitoes and other
insect pests.
   C.   Nuisance tree, plant or vegetation.
   D.   Vehicles on property when:
      1.   Dealer: There is an accumulation of more than eight (8) motor
vehicles or an equivalent amount of motor vehicle bodies or body parts on the
property and the owner of the property does not have a Malheur County zoning
permit and a license for a junk dealer, salvage yard, auto wrecking
establishment or commercial business; or
      2.   Hobbyist/Owner: There is an accumulation of more than eight (8)
motor vehicles or an equivalent amount of motor vehicle bodies or body parts on
the property and the motor vehicles are: a) not enclosed in a sight obscuring
fence not less than six feet (6') tall or a building that is maintained in good
condition, or b) not hidden or adequately screened by the terrain or other
natural objects, or by plantings or other appropriate means so as not to be
visible from public roads.
      3.   Exceptions: This subsection D does not apply to:
         a.   Any vehicle or equipment on property of a licensed or legitimate
business including an agricultural operation.
         b.   Any vehicle temporarily on property not to exceed ninety (90)
days. Nothing in this section is meant to permit commercial or temporary
activities that require a zoning permit or license.
         c.   Any vehicle on property when the vehicle is licensed, insured,
titled and actually and regularly operated on public roads.
         d.   Any vehicle operated on a regular or seasonal basis and is used
for the productivity, care and maintenance of the property or animals on the
property.
   E.   Unauthorized sewage disposal system.
   F.   Abandoned, dangerous or vacant building when the building or any
portion thereof is no longer used for its original purpose; is unsafe for its
intended purpose; a visual nuisance; or a risk to life, health, other property
or safety of the public or its occupants.
   G.   Noxious weeds 1 .
   H.   Violations of a continuous and ongoing nature of the Malheur County
open burning ordinance 2 .
   I.   Road hazards 3 .
   J.   Any other thing, act, omission or condition that is determined by a
county enforcement officer to meet the definition of nuisance.
   K.   A wireless telecommunication facility that is not in compliance with
its conditional use permit and requires removal because of discontinued or
nonuse.
   L.   Property placed on the Oregon health division "unfit for use list"
pursuant to ORS 453.879 because it has been used for the manufacture of illegal
drugs shall be considered a nuisance ninety (90) days after it has been listed
and shall remain a nuisance until such time as it is issued a "certificate of
fitness" by the Oregon health division.
   M.   Transporting waste or solid waste without a cover, tie down or suitable
security during transit so that no piece, article or portion of waste or solid
waste can blow, fall or otherwise be deposited upon public roads or the
property of another.
   N.   Salvaging any materials or solid waste disposed of at Lytle Boulevard
Landfill without authorization from the environmental health director.
   O.   Offensive littering.
   P.   Any property, whether vacant or improved, building, or accumulation of
waste or materials, which is infested or provides harborage for vector or
rodents. (Ord. 183, 10-7-2009)
 
Notes
1 1. See
  chapter 3  of this title.
2 2. See
  title 2, chapter 1  of this code.
3 3. See
  chapter 5  of this title.
3-4-5: NOTICE OF ABATEMENT:
   A.   Civil Infraction And Fine: Imposition of a civil infraction and fine
does not relieve an owner/responsible person of the duty to abate the nuisance.
The procedure to abate a nuisance is an additional remedy to the civil
infraction procedure. Abatement is not a defense to imposition of a forfeiture
or fine.
   B.   Abatement Of Noxious Weeds And Road Hazards: The abatement procedures
for noxious weeds are set out in ORS chapter 570 and
chapter 3 of this title. The abatement procedures for road hazards are set out
in ORS 368.251 to 368.281.
   C.   Notice Of Abatement (NOA): Upon determination that a public nuisance
exists as defined in this chapter or any other ordinance of the county, a
county enforcement officer shall notify the owner or responsible person(s) of
the nuisance in writing. The NOA shall be made by personal service, substituted
service, office service or by mail. Service by mail is to be by both first
class mail and by certified mail with return receipt requested. There shall be
a rebuttable presumption that any NOA sent by mail is delivered/served on the
third business day following deposit with the U.S. postal service.
   D.   Abatement By Owner Or Responsible Person: Within fourteen (14) days
after delivery of the NOA, the alleged offender, owner or responsible person
shall remove or abate the nuisance or meet with the county enforcement officer
to formulate a removal or abatement plan that is acceptable to the county.
   E.   Appeal Or Protest Notice Of Abatement:
      1.   Any person who receives a NOA may appeal from the NOA or protest
that a nuisance exists by filing with the justice court a written request for
an appeal or protest. The appeal or written protest shall be received by the
justice court within fourteen (14) days after the person appealing or
protesting received the NOA. The written request for an appeal or protest shall
contain a brief statement setting forth the facts of the appeal or protest and
in concise language the relief sought.
      2.   As soon as practical, the justice court shall fix a date, time and
place for the hearing on appeal. Such date shall not be less than ten (10) days
or more than sixty (60) days from the date the appeal was received by the
county. The hearing may be conducted by the justice of peace.
      3.   Failure of a person to file a timely appeal in accordance with the
provisions herein contained shall constitute a waiver of the right to a hearing
or adjudication of the NOA or any portion thereof.
      4.   All hearings shall be heard by the justice of peace and conducted in
such manner as to allow all interested persons full opportunity to be heard.
Hearings need not be conducted according to technical rules relating to
evidence and witnesses.
      5.   Following the hearing, the justice of peace may uphold, overrule or
modify any decision or requirement as set forth in the NOA.
      6.   A decision of the justice court after the hearing shall be final.
Appeal shall only be by writ of review under ORS chapter 34. (Ord. 183, 10-7-
2009)
3-4-6: ENFORCEMENT:
   A.   Any owner or responsible person who violates section
3-4-4 of this chapter shall be subject to a fine as set out in section
1-9A-3 of this code.
   B.   The county may institute any appropriate action to abate the nuisance
if the NOA or decision of the county court or justice of peace is not followed.
   C.   The enforcement officer, county representative or contractor hired by
the county may enter upon the property to abate the nuisance.
   D.   Accurate records of the direct expense incurred by the county to abate
the nuisance shall be kept and include a surcharge of ten percent (10%) of the
cost of abatement for administrative overhead.
   E.   At the conclusion of the abatement, a notice of costs of abatement
shall be served by a method that is consistent with ORCP 7(D). Payment must be
made within thirty (30) days from the date of the notice of costs of abatement.
   F.   The owner or responsible person may contest the charges at a hearing if
a written request for a hearing is received by the justice court within
fourteen (14) days after receipt of the notice of costs of abatement. The only
issue at the hearing shall be the reasonableness of the cost of abatement.
Failure of the person requesting the hearing shall constitute a waiver of the
right to present evidence at the hearing or thereafter. At the conclusion of
the hearing, the justice of peace shall issue an order detailing the amount of
the abatement cost the owner/responsible person must pay, if any. If costs are
not paid within thirty (30) days, the county may record a lien with the county
clerk lien record. The lien shall be foreclosed in the manner prescribed by
state law for the enforcement of liens against real property. Nine percent (9%)
interest per annum on the unpaid abatement costs shall run from the date of the
entry of the lien in the lien record. (Ord. 183, 10-7-2009)
CHAPTER 5
ROAD HAZARDS
SECTION:
3-5-1:   Obstruction Of Road Drains Prohibited
3-5-2:   Creation Of Road Hazard Prohibited
3-5-3:   Homeless Individuals Camping On County Right-Of-Way
3-5-1: OBSTRUCTION OF ROAD DRAINS PROHIBITED:
No person shall stop, obstruct or in any other manner impair or damage any
drain, ditch or other manmade or natural waterway that:
   A.   Prevents water from causing damage to, flowing across or standing on a
public road under County jurisdiction; or
   B.   Benefits a public road under County jurisdiction. (1989 Code)
3-5-2: CREATION OF ROAD HAZARD PROHIBITED:
Except as authorized by the County governing body, an owner or lawful occupant
of land shall not allow:
   A.   Any water to overflow, seep or otherwise discharge from that land onto
a public road under County jurisdiction including, but not limited to, water
that is passing over the land, diverted from the land by an obstruction on the
land, flowing from the land because of rainfall or discharged from an
irrigation sprinkler or other device.
   B.   Any structure, tree drainage way, soil deposit or other natural or
manmade thing on that land to present a danger to or create a hazard for the
public traveling on a public road or facilities within the right of way of the
public road by obstructing, hanging over or otherwise encroaching or
threatening to encroach in any manner on a public road that is under County
jurisdiction.
A person is not in violation of this Section if there is no reasonable method
for the person to control, stop or remove the cause of the violation. (1989
Code)
3-5-3:   HOMELESS INDIVIDUALS CAMPING ON COUNTY RIGHT-OF-WAY:
Camping is prohibited on County right-of-way as defined and set out in Malheur
County Code Title 3 Chapter 17. (Ord. 232, 6-21-2023)
CHAPTER 6
DOG CONTROL
SECTION:
3-6-1:   Dogs Running At Large
3-6-2:   Keeping Of Restricted Breeds Of Dogs
3-6-1: DOGS RUNNING AT LARGE:
   A.   No dog shall run at large in Malheur County. Any dog shall be
considered to be running at large when it is off or outside the premises
belonging to the owner or keeper of such dog, or not in the company of and
under the control of its owner or keeper, and does not include use of a dog:
      1.   Under the supervision of a person in order to legally hunt, chase or
tree wildlife;
      2.   To control or protect livestock; or
      3.   In other related agricultural activities.
   B.   The provisions of this section shall not apply to those areas inside a
city that has an established dog licensing program.
   C.   Nothing in this section shall limit the authority of any authorized
person to enforce the provisions of ORS 609.010 through 609.190. (1989 Code)
3-6-2: KEEPING OF RESTRICTED BREEDS OF DOGS:
   A.   Definitions:
   KEEPER: A person who keeps, owns, possesses, controls, harbors, exercises or
otherwise has charge of a restricted breed of dog.
   MUZZLE: A restraining device made of metal, plastic, leather or cloth or a
combination of these materials, that, when fitted and fastened over a snout/
mouth/head, prevents a dog from biting but allows room for the dog to breathe
and pant. The muzzle must be made in a manner that will not cause injury to the
dog or interfere with its vision or respiration, but must prevent the dog from
biting any person or animal.
   RESTRICTED BREED OF DOG: American pit bull terrier, American Staffordshire
terrier, Staffordshire bull terrier, American bulldog (Old Country bulldog),
Dogo Argentino, Canary dog (Canary Island dog, Presa Canario, Perro de Presa
Canario), Presa Mallorquin (Perro de Presa Mallorquin, Ca de Bou), Tosa (Tosa
inu, Tosa fighting dog, Japanese fighting dog, Japanese mastiff), Cane Corso
(Cane di Macellaio, Sicilian branchiero), Fila Brasileiro (Brazilian mastiff)
or any dog displaying the majority of physical traits or any one or more of the
above breeds, or any dog exhibiting those distinguishing characteristics which
substantially conform to the standards established by the American Kennel Club
or United Kennel Club for any of the above breeds. Any uncertainty about the
breed of a dog is to be determined by a duly licensed and qualified
veterinarian at the expense of the keeper.
   SECURE PEN, KENNEL OR ENCLOSURE: A five (5) sided structure designed to
prevent entry of a child or escape of a restricted breed of dog. The pen,
kennel or enclosure must have secure sides and a secure top. If the pen, kennel
or enclosure does not have a bottom secured to the sides, the sides must be
embedded in the ground no less than two feet (2'). All structures erected to
house a restricted breed of dog must comply with all zoning and building
regulations and ordinances of the county, be of adequate size and kept
sanitary. The gate of the pen, kennel or enclosure shall be secured with a
combination or key lock. (Note: If the pen is larger than 200 square feet or
has sides greater than 6 feet, the county may require a structural permit.
Inquiries are to be made at Inspections, Inc.)
   B.   Prohibited: It shall be unlawful for any person to have, own, possess,
keep, exercise control over, maintain, harbor or otherwise have charge of any
restricted breed of dog within Malheur County, unless the following guidelines
are complied with at the sole expense of the keeper. Failure to comply and
remain in compliance with all of the following guidelines shall subject the
restricted breed of dog to impoundment and the keeper to fines and other costs
as established by the Malheur County justice of the peace in accordance with
subsections D and E of this section:
      1.   At all times, a restricted breed of dog must be confined in
accordance with this chapter. When outside, a restricted breed of dog must be
in a secure pen, kennel or enclosure. No restricted breed of dog may be kept on
a porch, patio, or in any part of a house or structure that would allow the dog
to exit on its own volition. Restricted breeds of dogs shall not be leashed,
chained or otherwise attached to an inanimate object such as a tree, pole,
building or vehicle.
      2.   Restricted breeds of dogs that are being walked or exercised off the
premises of the owner must be muzzled and securely leashed with a leash no
longer than four feet (4') in length held by someone who is physically capable
of effectively controlling the dog.
      3.   Restricted breeds of dogs may not ride or be transported in an open
area of a truck or vehicle without a secure temporary enclosure. The temporary
transporting enclosure must have six (6) sides with a top and bottom that are
permanently attached to the sides except for the door for removal of the dog.
The enclosure must be of such material so that the dog cannot exit the
enclosure on its own.
      4.   The owner shall, at the owner's expense, have the restricted breed
of dog vaccinated for rabies as well as spayed and/or neutered and be able to
present proof that these procedures have been performed.
   C.   Exceptions: The prohibition and guidelines in subsection B of this
section shall not apply in the following circumstances.
      1.   A Humane Society or other nonprofit animal shelter.
      2.   A licensed business primarily intended to obtain a profit from the
kenneling of dogs.
      3.   A facility impounding dogs on behalf of Malheur County or a city
within Malheur County.
      4.   Law enforcement, animal control or Humane Society officials for the
purpose of carrying out this chapter or other dog control official business.
      5.   Any veterinarian while treating, grooming or housing a dog until
claimed by the owner.
      6.   Showing a restricted breed of dog in an exhibition, show or contest
sponsored by a dog club association or similar organization. However, the
sponsor of the exhibition, contest or show must receive authorization from the
Malheur County sheriff's office, must obtain applicable planning and zoning
approval and provide protective measures adequate to prevent restricted breeds
of dogs from escaping or injuring the public.
   D.   Impoundment:
      1.   If a restricted breed of dog has been impounded for violating this
section, the dog shall not be released from impoundment except on the order of
the justice of peace, but not less than three (3) days, excluding weekends and
holidays, subsequent to the owner being notified or reasonable efforts have
been made to notify the owner of the impoundment. Possession of the dog may be
recovered by the dog's owner if the judge finds that the restricted breed of
dog was not in violation of this section, or upon payment of all assessments,
expenses, fees or costs as set forth in subsection E of this section and upon
proof of compliance with the guidelines set forth in subsection B of this
section. If possession of the dog is not recovered in the time frame ordered by
the justice of peace or an owner cannot reasonably be located, the dog shall be
deemed an unclaimed dog and may be disposed of by adoption or death in a humane
manner.
   E.   Infraction: Violations of this section are a class B infraction under
this code and subject to a monetary assessment of no more than five hundred
dollars ($500.00). Monetary assessments shall be two hundred fifty dollars
($250.00) for the first offense and five hundred dollars ($500.00) for each
subsequent offense plus the expense of boarding, reclamation fees, food and
necessary veterinary expenses. This assessment may be imposed in addition to
impoundment and court ordered disposition of the dog as set forth in subsection
D of this section. (Ord. 161, 12-13-2006)
CHAPTER 7
AMBULANCE AND EMERGENCY MEDICAL SERVICES
SECTION:
3-7-1:   Short Title And Authority
3-7-2:   Policy And Purpose
3-7-3:   Definitions
3-7-4:   Emergency Medical Service Advisory Board (Rep. by Ord. 127, 7-25-2000)
3-7-5:   Ambulance And Emergency Medical Service Areas
3-7-5-1:   Ambulance Service Areas Adopted
3-7-6:   Duties Of Ambulance Service Provider (Rep. by Ord. 127, 7-25-2000)
3-7-7:   Emergency Services Director (Rep. by Ord. 127, 7-25-2000)
3-7-8:   EMS Medical Director/Supervising Physician
3-7-1: SHORT TITLE AND AUTHORITY:
   A.   Title: This chapter shall be known as the MALHEUR COUNTY AMBULANCE AND
EMERGENCY MEDICAL SERVICE ORDINANCE. (1998 Revision)
   B.   Authority: This chapter is enacted pursuant to ORS 682.205, 682.275 and
203.035. (Ord. 127, 7-25-2000)
3-7-2: POLICY AND PURPOSE:
The county court finds:
   A.   That ORS 682.205 requires Malheur County to develop a plan for the
county relating to the need for and coordination of ambulance and emergency
medical services and to establish ambulance service areas consistent with the
county ASA plan to provide efficient and effective ambulance services. (1998
Revision)
   B.   This chapter, which establishes ambulance and emergency medical service
areas, together with the documentation known as the Malheur County ambulance
service area plan (ASA plan) incorporated herein by reference, make up the
complete plan for ambulance and emergency medical service for Malheur County.
(Ord. 127, 7-25-2000)
   C.   It is the intent of this chapter that no disruption of services occur.
Any agreements to provide services in effect on the date this chapter becomes
effective shall remain in effect thereafter.
   D.   It is also the intent of this chapter to provide the most efficient and
effective EMS system possible, while still maintaining each EMS provider's
independence and identity. (1998 Revision)
   E.   An EMS medical director/supervising physician shall be appointed for
all EMS providers within Malheur County. This chapter gives the EMS medical
director/supervising physician all powers and duties under ORS 682.245(4) and
OAR 847-35-0025. (Ord. 127, 7-25-2000)
3-7-3: DEFINITIONS:
The words and phrases in this chapter shall have the meanings provided in ORS
chapter 682, OAR chapter 333, division 260 and OAR chapter 847, division 35.
(Ord. 127, 7-25-2000)
3-7-4: EMERGENCY MEDICAL SERVICE ADVISORY BOARD:
(Rep. by Ord. 127, 7-25-2000)
3-7-5: AMBULANCE AND EMERGENCY MEDICAL SERVICE AREAS:
3-7-5-1: AMBULANCE SERVICE AREAS ADOPTED:
For the efficient and effective provision of ambulance and emergency medical
services in accordance with the 1998 ASA plan, the ambulance and emergency
medical service areas shown on the map included in the ASA plan are hereby
adopted as the ambulance service areas for Malheur County. The county court, by
ordinance and pursuant to ORS 682.205, may adjust the boundaries of the
ambulance service areas from time to time as necessary to provide efficient and
effective ambulance services, as provided in this chapter. (Ord. 127, 7-25-
2000)
3-7-6: DUTIES OF AMBULANCE SERVICE PROVIDER:
(Rep. by Ord. 127, 7-25-2000)
3-7-7: EMERGENCY SERVICES DIRECTOR:
(Rep. by Ord. 127, 7-25-2000)
3-7-8: EMS MEDICAL DIRECTOR/SUPERVISING PHYSICIAN:
The EMS medical director/supervising physician shall have all powers and duties
under ORS 682.245(4) and OAR 847-35-0025, including final authority for all
protocols and standing orders which pertain to patient care. (Ord. 127, 7-25-
2000)

FOOD HANDLER'S CERTIFICATION

CHAPTER 9
TRAFFIC SAFETY
SECTION:
3-9-1:   Short Title And Authority
3-9-2:   Policy And Purpose
3-9-3:   Malheur County Traffic Safety Commission
3-9-3-1:   Commission Created; Members' Terms; Organization
3-9-3-2:   Powers And Duties
3-9-1: SHORT TITLE AND AUTHORITY:
   A.   Title: This chapter shall be known as the MALHEUR COUNTY TRAFFIC SAFETY
ORDINANCE.
   B.   Authority: This chapter is enacted pursuant to ORS 203.035 and 802.329.
(Ord. 74, 4-2-1991)
3-9-2: POLICY AND PURPOSE:
The county court finds:
   A.   That ORS 802.329 provides that Malheur County may participate in the
state's highway safety program. (Ord. 74, 4-2-1991)
   B.   That reducing Malheur County's motor vehicle crash rate will save
valuable lives and limbs and will reduce insurance rates for motor vehicles
registered in Malheur County, including those owned and operated by Malheur
County. (Ord. 162, 1-17-2007)
3-9-3: MALHEUR COUNTY TRAFFIC SAFETY COMMISSION:
3-9-3-1: COMMISSION CREATED; MEMBERS' TERMS; ORGANIZATION:
There is hereby created a Malheur County traffic safety commission, each member
of which shall be appointed by the county court for a two (2) year term. There
is no limit to the number of subsequent terms each member may be appointed to
serve. The commission shall choose its own chairperson and secretary and shall
meet at least quarterly or when called upon by the county court. Motions shall
be passed by a majority of those attending. (Ord. 96, 1-2-1996)
The commission shall consist of:
   A.   One representative of the Malheur County health department.
   B.   One representative of the fire services from within Malheur County.
   C.   One representative of the Malheur County sheriff's office, one
representative of the Nyssa police department, one representative from the
Ontario police department and one representative from the Oregon state police
department.
   D.   One representative from the Malheur County road department, one
representative from the Ontario road assessment district, one representative
from the Nyssa road assessment district, one representative from each of the
city public works and one representative from ODOT.
   E.   One representative from the Malheur County district attorney's office.
   F.   The Malheur County justice of the peace.
   G.   One representative of the Malheur County private business community.
   H.   One representative who has either a special interest or experience in
traffic safety issues. (Ord. 162, 1-17-2007)
   I.   One representative of Malheur County's students. (Ord. 199, 4-3-2013)
   J.   One representative from a trucking or towing business that has its
principal place of business in Malheur County. (Ord. 162, 1-17-2007)
The Malheur County counsel shall provide legal advice and assistance to the
commission as needed. (Ord. 96, 1-2-1996)
3-9-3-2: POWERS AND DUTIES:
The commission's powers and duties to identify and meet Malheur County's
traffic and safety needs include, but are not limited to, the following: (Ord.
74, 4-2-1991)
   A.   To review traffic crash reports made to the motor vehicle division,
Oregon department of transportation, which the law makes available to the
commission, and to initiate measures which will help prevent crashes in the
future. (Ord. 162, 1-17-2007)
   B.   To solicit input from throughout Malheur County concerning traffic
safety issues and problems.
   C.   To make the commission the countywide focal point and clearinghouse for
traffic safety issues.
   D.   To facilitate communication and public relations about traffic safety
issues regionwide. (Ord. 74, 4-2-1991)
   E.   To coordinate available resources and programming made available for
traffic safety, engineering, education and enforcement countywide. (Ord. 162,
1-17-2007)
   F.   To act as the countywide resource for accessing state and federal
monies for traffic safety programs.
   G.   To encourage the development and implementation of new projects in
traffic safety.
   H.   To recognize accomplishment in local traffic safety efforts in diverse
areas. (Ord. 74, 4-2-1991)
CHAPTER 10
EMERGENCY MANAGEMENT
SECTION:
3-10-1:   Title; Authority
3-10-2:   Policy And Purpose
3-10-3:   Definitions
3-10-4:   Emergency Services Director
3-10-5:   Emergency Declaration
3-10-6:   Enforcement And Penalties
3-10-1: TITLE; AUTHORITY:
   A.   Title: This Chapter shall be known as the MALHEUR COUNTY EMERGENCY
MANAGEMENT ORDINANCE.
   B.   Authority: This Chapter is enacted pursuant to ORS 401.015 et seq.
(Ord. 95, 11-21-1995)
3-10-2: POLICY AND PURPOSE:
The Malheur County Court finds:
   A.   ORS Chapter 401 requires counties to establish an emergency management
agency. An emergency management agency is necessary to prevent, prepare for,
respond to, and recover from damage resulting from a disaster.
   B.   A disaster could occur at any time and a local agency for emergency
management is necessary to protect the general welfare of the people of Malheur
County.
   C.   It is necessary to designate an Emergency Services Director for the
County and give the Director all powers and duties under ORS 401.305.
   D.   The purpose of this Chapter is to provide for an organization to act
before, during and after an emergency or disaster to coordinate mitigation,
preparedness, response and recovery from disaster. (Ord. 95, 11-21-1995)
3-10-3: DEFINITIONS:
The words and phrases in this Chapter shall have the meanings provided in ORS,
Chapter 401, as currently constituted unless specifically defined herein to
have a different meaning.
"Emergency" includes any manmade or natural event or circumstances causing or
threatening loss of life, injury to person or property, human suffering, or
weather, drought, earthquake, volcanic activity, spills or releases of oil or
hazardous material as defined in ORS 466.605, contamination, utility or
transportation emergencies, disease, blight, infestation, crisis influx of
migrants unmanageable by the County, civil disturbance, riot, sabotage and war.
(Ord. 95, 11-21-1995)
3-10-4: EMERGENCY SERVICES DIRECTOR:
The Director of Emergency Services is hereby appointed as the person who shall
have the responsibility for the organization, administration, and operations of
the Malheur County Emergency Management Agency, subject to the direction of the
Malheur County Court, as specified in ORS 401.305. (Ord. 95, 11-21-1995)
3-10-5: EMERGENCY DECLARATION:
   A.   When in the judgment and discretion of the County Court a state of
emergency exists, the Court shall declare in writing and publicize the
existence of the same. If the circumstances prohibit the timely action of the
County Court, any combination of two (2) of the following Malheur County
officials may together declare such a state of emergency: the County Court
Judge, and County Court Commissioner, the County Sheriff, or the Emergency
Services Director. This declaration shall be in effect for a period of up to
seven (7) days, at which time the County Court will either continue or
discontinue the state of emergency.
   B.   The Emergency Services Director shall cause an Emergency Operations
Plan to be prepared, adopted, maintained, and exercised. The Emergency
Operations Plan shall provide for an organization for emergency management,
including a chain of command, the use of Incident Command System, management
and maintenance of an Emergency Operations Center, and for the operations
during and after the state of emergency.
   C.   Whenever a state of emergency has been declared to exist within the
County, as authorized pursuant to ORS Chapter 401 and by executive order of the
Governor, certain extraordinary measures may be taken in the interest of public
health, safety, or welfare. These measures may be taken by the County Court. If
the circumstances prohibit the timely action of the Court, any combination of
two (2) of the following Malheur County officials may together implement these
actions for a period of seven (7) days, unless continued by the County Court:
the County Court Judge, a County Court Commissioner, the County Sheriff, or the
Emergency Services Director. (Ord. 95, 11-21-1995)
3-10-6: ENFORCEMENT AND PENALTIES:
Any such person who violates any of the provisions of this Chapter is guilty of
a Class A County infraction. Failure to comply with any provision of this
Chapter shall be a separate offense for each provision. (Ord. 95, 11-21-1995)
CHAPTER 11
BOVINE TRICHOMONIASIS TESTING
SECTION:
3-11-1:   Purpose
3-11-2:   Definitions
3-11-3:   Bulls In Public Grazing Allotments
3-11-4:   Virgin Bulls
3-11-5:   Trichomoniasis Test Tag And Virgin Bull Identification Tag
3-11-6:   Penalties
3-11-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to control the bovine venereal disease
trichomoniasis. The requirements of this chapter are in addition to Oregon
state law. The provisions of the bovine trichomoniasis test positive response
program, otherwise applicable to positive trichomoniasis cases, shall apply.
(Ord. 154, 4-5-2006, eff. 9-1-2006)
3-11-2: DEFINITIONS:
   BOVINE TRICHOMONIASIS OR TRICHOMONIASIS: A sexually transmitted disease of
cattle caused by the parasitic protozoan organism Trichomoniasis fetus.
   OFFICIAL TRICHOMONIASIS TAG: An ear tag of the correct color for the then
current trichomoniasis testing season as designated by the Oregon department of
agriculture to be the official Oregon trich ear tag. Bulls which bear a current
trichomoniasis test tag from another state that has an official trichomoniasis
testing program will be acceptable to Malheur County as an official
trichomoniasis tag.
   TRICHOMONIASIS TESTING SEASON: The period from September 1 through August 31
each year and representative of the year starting January 1 as the current
trichomoniasis testing year.
   VETERINARIAN: A person who holds a current and valid license to practice
veterinary medicine in Oregon or in the state where the veterinarian practices
and who is either certified under OAR 603-011-0630 or otherwise trained to
perform trichomoniasis testing and diagnosis.
   VIRGIN BULL: A sexually intact male bovine less than twelve (12) months of
age that is certified by an owner or the owner's representative as having had
no potential breeding contact with females. Certification by an owner or the
owner's representative shall be a written instrument signed by the owner or the
owner's representative that the bull is a virgin bull. (Ord. 154, 4-5-2006,
eff. 9-1-2006; amd. Ord. 188, 11-3-2010)
3-11-3: BULLS IN PUBLIC GRAZING ALLOTMENTS:
Bulls that are turned out on public grazing allotments, that are located wholly
or partially within Malheur County, shall be tested for trichomoniasis by a
veterinarian before March 31 of each trichomoniasis testing season or forty
five (45) days prior to turnout on a public grazing allotment, whichever occurs
first. (Ord. 154, 4-5-2006, eff. 9-1-2006)
3-11-4: VIRGIN BULLS:
Virgin bulls shall be exempt from the trichomoniasis testing requirement in
this chapter. (Ord. 154, 4-5-2006, eff. 9-1-2006)
3-11-5: TRICHOMONIASIS TEST TAG AND VIRGIN BULL IDENTIFICATION TAG:
All bulls tested for trichomoniasis or certified as virgin bulls turned out on
public grazing allotments, located wholly or partially within Malheur County,
shall be identified with an official trichomoniasis tag. Bulls tested by a
veterinarian in Oregon must be recorded on the Oregon state trich testing/
tagging form. (Ord. 154, 4-5-2006, eff. 9-1-2006)
3-11-6: PENALTIES:
Violation of this chapter is a Malheur County code class B infraction with an
assessment of two hundred fifty dollars ($250.00) per bull. (Ord. 154, 4-5-
2006, eff. 9-1-2006)
CHAPTER 12
DESIGNATION OF CRIMINAL GANG AFFILIATES
SECTION:
3-12-1:   Definitions
3-12-2:   Procedure
3-12-3:   Hearings Process
3-12-4:   Records Division
3-12-5:   Appeals Of Existing Designations
3-12-6:   Purge Process
3-12-7:   Improper Designation
3-12-1: DEFINITIONS:
   CRIMINAL GANG: A gang is criminal if individuals affiliated with it have
committed two (2) or more crimes, which involve any of the following:
   A.   Benefit members of the gang;
   B.   Are committed as part of an initiation process or membership ritual;
   C.   Are designed to announce the existence of the gang, its membership or
its territorial claims;
   D.   Are committed in response to the race, color, religion, sexual
preference, national origin or gang association of the victim; or
   E.   Are designed to intimidate a victim in the name of the gang.
   CRIMINAL GANG AFFILIATE (OR AFFILIATE OF A CRIMINAL GANG): A person who
participates in the activity of a criminal gang, or who actively pursues
membership in a criminal gang. A person will be designated as a criminal gang
affiliate only when there is clear and convincing evidence that the person has
been a criminal gang affiliate in the previous three (3) years, and while a
criminal gang affiliate, either one of the indicators in list A of this
definition was present, or two (2) of the indicators in list B of this
definition were present.
   A.   List A (1 of 3 required):
      1.   The person admits or asserts affiliation, membership or
participation with a criminal gang.
      2.   The person participates in a criminal gang initiation, ritual or
ceremony.
      3.   The person conspires to commit, or commits a crime:
         a.   Which is part of a pattern of street crimes facilitated by the
efforts of other criminal gang affiliates, which advance the interests of the
person or criminal gang; or
         b.   To attract the attention of the criminal gang or enhance the
standing of the person with the criminal gang; or
         c.   For the benefit of the criminal gang; or
         d.   To announce the existence of the criminal gang, its membership or
its territorial claims; or
         e.   In response to the race, color, religion, sexual preference,
national origin or criminal gang association of the victim.
   B.   List B (2 of 7 required):
      1.   The person displays knowledge of the gang's history, leadership,
activities or rituals in a context that clearly indicates affiliation with the
criminal gang; or
      2.   The person announces to the police that the person is willing to
commit assaults, crimes, or make other sacrifices for the criminal gang; or
      3.   The person wears clothes or jewelry unique to a gang in a context
that clearly indicates affiliation with a criminal gang; or
      4.   The person uses a hand sign or language, which, due to content or
context, clearly indicates affiliation with the criminal gang; or
      5.   The person's name appears on a criminal street gang document; or
      6.   The person is in a photograph with other people who collectively
display criminal gang signs or apparel to exhibit solidarity; or
      7.   The person possesses a criminal gang tattoo.
   GANG: An ongoing organization, association or group of three (3) or more
individuals who utilize both of the following:
   A.   Use a gang name, common identifying sign or symbol, or acknowledge an
identifiable leadership; and
   B.   Have a high rate of interaction among themselves to the exclusion of
other persons or gangs. (Ord. 164, 2-21-2007)
3-12-2: PROCEDURE:
   A.   Designation Request By Law Enforcement Officer: Any law enforcement
officer may request that a person be designated as a criminal gang affiliate by
describing, in a report, the specific conduct that corresponds to the criminal
gang affiliation indicators listed above. Any designation request must contain
a reference date which corresponds to the last incident of occurrence relied on
for designation. This reference date will determine the purge date of the
designation; therefore, all reports of conduct must document the date of the
conduct. If the report refers to a resident of Malheur County (exclusive of the
incorporated cities) or if the conduct that corresponds to the criminal gang
affiliation indicators listed above occurred in Malheur County, the report must
be routed to the Malheur County sheriff.
   B.   Designation Recommended By Malheur County Sheriff: The sheriff or his/
her designee will review all requests for criminal gang affiliation designation
and will recommend whether or not the request should result in designation. The
sheriff may not recommend designation unless:
      1.   There is clear and convincing evidence that the person presents at
least one of the indicators from list A in section
3-12-1 of this chapter and/or two (2) indicators from list B in section
3-12-1 of this chapter within the previous three (3) years, and
      2.   There is clear and convincing evidence the person is affiliated with
a criminal gang.
   C.   Notice To Potential Designee:
      1.   Personal Notice Or Notice By Both Certified, Return Receipt And
Regular Mail: If the sheriff recommends that a person be designated as a
criminal gang affiliate, the sheriff or his/her designee will provide written
notice of the recommendation to the potential designee either by delivery in
person or delivery by both certified, return receipt mail and regular mail to
the last known address of the person. The sheriff or his/her designee will make
reasonable efforts to determine the potential designee's last known address
including, but not limited to, a search of LEDS, Oregon DMV files and Oregon
parole and probation records. In the event the potential designee is a
juvenile, both the juvenile and a parent or guardian of the juvenile will be
delivered with written notice of the recommendation either in person or by both
certified, return receipt mail and regular mail. The sheriff or his/her
designee may request a search of the Malheur County juvenile department's
probation records to determine a juvenile's last known address. If notice is
provided in person, the deputy sheriff delivering notice will document the
date, place and time personal notice was delivered.
      2.   Content Of Notice: The notice will include a list of the indicator
(s) relied on to recommend designation, and will state that supporting
documentation, if any, may be viewed by the potential designee and in the event
the potential designee is a juvenile, documentation may be viewed by both the
juvenile and his/her parent(s) or guardian(s) at the sheriff's office located
at 151 B. Street West, Vale. There will be no charge for this service. Copies
of supporting documentation may be provided at a reasonable cost, as
established by the sheriff's office. The notice will prominently announce that
the recommendation will result in a designation of the person as a criminal
gang affiliate in fourteen (14) calendar days from the date of personal
notification or from mailing of the notice. If the potential designee wishes to
contest the designation, the potential designee must request a hearing in
writing which must be received at the sheriff's office no later than fourteen
(14) calendar days from the date of personal notification or from mailing of
the notice. If a potential designee does not request a hearing, the sheriff
will send the recommendation for designation to the district attorney for
review.
The notice will also describe the hearing and appeal process set out below.
      3.   Undeliverable Notice: The sheriff will place notice letters, which
are returned undeliverable in the designation file, and designation will occur
in accordance with this chapter.
      4.   List Of Pending Designations: A list of pending designations with
the sheriff will be maintained at the sheriff's office. Upon request, any
person will be told whether he/she is on the list of pending designations, and
parents or guardians will be told if their children or wards are on the list.
(Ord. 164, 2-21-2007)
3-12-3: HEARINGS PROCESS:
   A.   First Stage Hearing Before Sheriff: The first stage hearing will occur
within twenty one (21) calendar days of receipt of a request for a hearing. The
sheriff or his/her designee will try to accommodate the schedule of the
potential designee (and parent or guardian in the event the person is a
juvenile). The sheriff or his/her designee reserves the right to set the time
and date of the hearing in the event a mutually convenient time and date cannot
be easily accommodated. At the hearing, the potential designee may present any
information that bears on the applicability of the designation criteria, and
will be required to provide a current address. Hearings will be tape recorded
at the discretion of the sheriff or his/her designee. Hearings may be held
telephonically or by correspondence at the discretion of the sheriff and upon
request of the potential designee. Any decision following the first stage
hearing will be made at the end of the hearing orally in front of the potential
designee or at a later date by regular, first class mail to the current address
provided by the potential designee. A record of the date of mailing of the
decision must be maintained in the sheriff's office.
   B.   Second Stage Hearing Before County Court Judge: If the sheriff
continues to recommend designation as a criminal gang affiliate following the
first stage hearing, the potential designee may request a second stage hearing
before the Malheur County judge or his/her designee which may not be the
hearing officer involved in the first stage hearing. A request for a second
stage hearing must be made in writing and received by the Malheur County judge
at 251 B. Street West, Vale, OR 97918, within fourteen (14) calendar days
following the date of the first hearing if an oral decision is made at the end
