of first hearing or within fourteen (14) calendar days following the mailing of
a written decision from the first hearing. A second stage hearing will be
conducted within twenty one (21) calendar days from receipt of the written
request. The county judge or his/her designee will try to accommodate the
schedule of the potential designee (and parent or guardian in the event the
person is a juvenile). The county judge or his/her designee reserves the right
to set the time and date of the hearing in the event a mutually convenient time
and date cannot be easily accommodated. Hearings at the second stage will be
held de novo. At the hearing, the potential designee may present any
information that bears on the applicability of the designation criteria, and
will be required to provide a current address. Hearings will be tape recorded
at the discretion of the county judge or his/her designee. Hearings may be held
telephonically or by correspondence at the discretion of the county judge and
upon request of the potential designee. Any decision following the second stage
hearing will be made at the end of the hearing orally in front of the potential
designee or at a later date by regular, first class mail to the current address
provided by the potential designee. A record of the date of mailing of the
decision must be maintained in the county judge's office.
   C.   Final Appeals Process:
      1.   Review And Determination By District Attorney: Following the second
stage hearing, if the potential designee wishes to contest the recommended
designation, the potential designee must request review by the district
attorney. A request for review must be in writing and received by the district
attorney at 251 B. Street West, Vale, OR 97918, within fourteen (14) calendar
days from the date of the second hearing if at the end of the second hearing an
oral decision is made or within fourteen (14) calendar days from the date the
written decision from the second hearing is mailed to the potential designee.
The district attorney will review any information submitted at both hearings
and determine, without a hearing, whether gang affiliation designation is
supported by clear and convincing evidence and meets the stated criteria in
this chapter. The potential designee will be informed of the decision by letter
mailed regular, first class mail to the current address of the potential
designee as provided by the potential designee. If the district attorney
designates as a criminal gang affiliate, the decision will become effective
immediately upon mailing of his/her determination unless the potential designee
appeals the determination to the Malheur County justice court. The district
attorney's determination will list the steps a potential designee may take to
appeal the determination to the Malheur County justice court. The district
attorney's office will maintain a record of when the determination was mailed
to the potential designee.
      2.   Appeal To Malheur County Justice Court: A notice of appeal from the
district attorney's determination must be received by the Malheur County
justice court currently at 1178 SW Fourth Street, Ontario, OR 97914, in writing
within fourteen (14) calendar days of the date the determination was mailed to
the potential designee. On receipt of a written request for appeal the Malheur
County justice court will schedule an appeal hearing and will notify the
district attorney and the potential designee of a hearing date. The hearing
will be held de novo. Oral evidence shall be taken only on oath or affirmation.
Hearsay evidence may be used for the purpose of supplementing or explaining any
direct evidence, but shall not be sufficient in itself to support a finding
unless it would be admissible over objection in civil actions in courts of
competent jurisdiction. Any relevant evidence shall be admitted. The potential
designee shall have the right to present evidence and witnesses, to cross
examine witnesses who testify against him or her and to submit rebuttal
evidence. Telephonic or hearings conducted by correspondence may be allowed if
a hardship exists at the discretion of the justice of peace and at the request
of the potential designee. Following the hearing, the Malheur County justice of
peace will notify both the district attorney and the potential designee of his/
her decision in writing or orally upon the conclusion of the hearing. If the
Malheur justice of peace upholds the determination, the district attorney may
list the person as a criminal gang affiliate in his/her records.
   D.   Right To Counsel: At any and all hearings, the potential designee may
be represented by counsel. (Ord. 164, 2-21-2007)
3-12-4: RECORDS DIVISION:
The district attorney will review all recommendations for criminal gang
affiliation designation to ensure Malheur County's criteria are met. If the
documentation presented to the district attorney supports designation, the
record of the person will be updated to reflect criminal gang affiliation
designation. Any designation must contain a reference date which corresponds to
the last incident of occurrence relied on for designation. This reference date
will determine the purge date of the designation. If the documented conduct
does not support designation, the record of the person will not be updated and
a form indicating the deficiency of documentation will be sent to the sheriff.
(Ord. 164, 2-21-2007)
3-12-5: APPEALS OF EXISTING DESIGNATIONS:
Any person on the criminal gang affiliate list will be provided a hearing to
challenge the designation if:
   A.   The person has not previously brought a challenge to the designation;
and
   B.   The person submits clear and convincing evidence that she/he was not
properly notified in accordance with this chapter before being designated and
listed as a criminal gang affiliate.
All challenges to existing designations processed by the sheriff will be routed
to the sheriff for processing. Upon receipt of a valid challenge to an existing
designation, a hearing will be set up within twenty one (21) calendar days. The
hearings and subsequent final appeal process as set forth above will be
followed. (Ord. 164, 2-21-2007)
3-12-6: PURGE PROCESS:
The criminal gang affiliate designation will expire four (4) years after the
incident on which it is based. If during this four (4) year period the criminal
gang affiliate engages in conduct or behavior that meets the designation
criteria, the person may be redesignated by means of the notice, hearing and
appeals process set forth above.
Each month the district attorney will publish and distribute a list of
individuals on the criminal gang affiliate designation list with the date the
record is to be purged. Law enforcement agencies having information that will
support a redesignation of the person as a criminal gang affiliate must send
out notice of the redesignation pursuant to the notice, hearings and appeal
process set forth above. (Ord. 164, 2-21-2007)
3-12-7: IMPROPER DESIGNATION:
In the event a person is improperly designated as a criminal gang affiliate,
the sheriff may submit a special report to the district attorney requesting to
rescind the designation. The district attorney will review the information
submitted and if appropriate the district attorney will remove the designation.
(Ord. 164, 2-21-2007)
CHAPTER 13
PROHIBITED SUBSTANCES
SECTION:
3-13-1:   Unlawful Intoxicating Chemical Compounds
3-13-1: UNLAWFUL INTOXICATING CHEMICAL COMPOUNDS:
   A.   It shall be unlawful for any person, including a corporation or other
entity, to manufacture, distribute, dispense, ingest, use, possess, purchase,
attempt to purchase, sell, publicly display for sale, attempt to sell, give,
trade or barter, any one or more of the following chemical compounds and/or
substances, including their salts, isomers, homologues and salts of their
isomers and homologues:
      1.   Salvia divinorum or Salvinorum A; all parts of the plant presently
classified botanically as Salvia divinorum, whether growing or not, the seeds
thereof, any extract from any part of such plant, and every compound,
manufacture, salts derivative, mixture or preparation of such plant, its seeds
or extracts;
      2.   1-Pentyl-3-(1-naphthoyl)indole (also known as JWH-018);
      3.   2-(3-hydroxycyclohexyl)-5-(2-methyloctan-2-yl)phenol (also known as
CP-47/497), and the dimethylhexyl, dimethyloctyl and dimethylnonyl homologues
of CP-47/497;
      4.   1-Butyl-3-(1-naphthoyl)indole (also known as JWH-073);
      5.   1-(2-(4-(morpholinyl)ethyl))-3-(1-naphthoyl)indole (also known as
JWH-200);
      6.   1-Pentyl-3-(2-methoxyphenylacetyl)indole (also known as JWH-250);
      7.   1-Hexyl-3-(1-naphthoyl)indole (also known as JWH-019);
      8.   1-Pentyl-3-(4-chloro-1-naphthoyl)indole (also known as JWH-398);
      9.   1-(3-trifluoromethylphenyl) piperazine (also known as TFMPP);
      10.   Any similar structural analogs of the above chemical compounds;
      11.   Any other synthetic cannabinoids;
      12.   Any commercial products sold as aromatics or incense under the
brand names spice, black mamba, K2, puff, smoke, skunk, pandora potpourri and
sugar sticks or other brand names, that have been determined by chemical
testing laboratories, law enforcement or other governmental agencies to contain
any of the foregoing compounds; (Ord. 190, 10-13-2010)
      13.   Mephedrone (2-methylamino-1-p-tolylpropan-1-one) also known as 4-
methylmethcathinone (4-MMC), 4-methylephedrone;
      14.   3,4-Methylenedioxypyrovalerone (MDPV). (Res. R11-2, 2-2-2011)
   B.   The Malheur County court may by resolution add to or amend the list of
unlawful intoxicating compounds identified in subsection A of this section.
   C.   It is not a violation of subsection A of this section if the person was
acting at the direction of an authorized agent of Malheur County to enforce or
ensure compliance with this law prohibiting the sale of the aforementioned
intoxicating chemical compound.
   D.   If any of the intoxicating chemical compounds prohibited herein are
found in the possession of any person, they may be confiscated and destroyed by
law enforcement officials.
   E.   This section shall not apply to drugs or substances lawfully prescribed
or to drugs or substances which have been approved by the federal food and drug
administration or which are specifically permitted by Oregon law.
   F.   A violation of subsection A of this section is a class A violation
under
title 1, chapter 9, article A, "General Enforcement Provisions", of this code.
Each day on which a violation occurs shall be punishable as a separate
violation.
   G.   Malheur County shall have the authority to seek an injunction against
any person or business violating subsection A of this section. In any action
seeking an injunction Malheur County shall be entitled to collect its
enforcement expenses, including reasonable attorney fees incurred at trial and
on appeal. (Ord. 190, 10-13-2010)
CHAPTER 14
PROHIBITED ACTIVITIES RELATED TO MARIJUANA
Editor's Note: Ordinance 229 will become effective only if Ordinance 210 is
repealed.
SECTION:
3-14-1:   Provisions
3-14-2:   Fine For Violation
3-14-3:   Civil Action
3-14-4:   Severability
3-14-5:   Emergency Clause
3-14-1: PROVISIONS:
The establishment or maintenance of any one or more of the following is
prohibited within the jurisdictional limits of Malheur County:
   A.   Marijuana processing sites registered under section 85, chapter 614,
Oregon laws 2015;
   B.   Medical marijuana dispensaries registered under ORS 475.314;
   C.   Marijuana producers licensed under section 19, chapter 1, Oregon laws
2015;
   D.   Marijuana processors licensed under section 20, chapter 1, Oregon laws
2015;
   E.   Marijuana wholesalers licensed under section 21, chapter 1, Oregon laws
2015; and
   F.   Marijuana retailers licensed under section 22, chapter 1, Oregon laws
2015; and
   G.   Any combination of the entities described above or under section 133 of
house bill 3400 (2015). (Ord. 210, 8-5-2015)
3-14-2: FINE FOR VIOLATION:
A violation of this section is a class A violation under
title 1, chapter 9, article A, "General Enforcement Provisions", of this code.
Each day such violation continues shall be considered a separate violation.
(Ord. 210, 8-5-2015)
3-14-3: CIVIL ACTION:
In addition to, or in lieu of, the imposition of a fine, Malheur County may
initiate a civil action against any person or entity violating this chapter for
any and all remedies available under Oregon law, including, but not limited to,
obtaining mandatory and prohibitory injunctions and orders of abatement.
Malheur County shall be entitled to collect its costs and expenses, including
reasonable attorney fees incurred at trial, hearing or on appeal. (Ord. 210, 8-
5-2015)
3-14-4: SEVERABILITY:
If any part or section of this chapter is invalid or unenforceable in any
respect for any reason, the validity and enforceability of any such provision
in any other respect and of the remaining provisions of this chapter shall not
be in any way impaired. (Ord. 210, 8-5-2015)
3-14-5: EMERGENCY CLAUSE:
The Malheur County court hereby adjudges that it is necessary for the immediate
preservation of the peace, health, and safety of the county that this chapter
shall take effect immediately upon its passage and approval, and an emergency
is hereby declared to exist and this chapter shall be in full force and effect
immediately upon its passage. (Ord. 210, 8-5-2015)
CHAPTER 15
POSSESSION OF MARIJUANA PROHIBITED ON COUNTY PROPERTY
SECTION:
3-15-1:   County Property And Facilities
3-15-2:   Possession Not Applicable To Law Enforcement
3-15-3:   Fine For Violation
3-15-4:   Civil Action
3-15-5:   Severability
3-15-6:   Emergency Clause
3-15-1: COUNTY PROPERTY AND FACILITIES:
The consumption, use, display, possession, transfer, distribution, sale or
growth of marijuana on county owned or operated property or facilities is
prohibited. Such county property and facilities includes, but is not limited
to: Cow Hollow Park, Bully Creek Park, Malheur County Courthouse, Malheur
County justice court, Malheur County Fairgrounds, health department, Community
Corrections, Veterans Services, sheriff offices, road department facilities,
extension office, county offices and associated parking areas, county vehicles,
and all other real or personal property owned or operated by Malheur County.
(Ord. 211, 8-5-2015)
3-15-2: POSSESSION NOT APPLICABLE TO LAW ENFORCEMENT:
Law enforcement officials may possess marijuana on county property and
facilities within their official employment capacity. (Ord. 211, 8-5-2015)
3-15-3: FINE FOR VIOLATION:
A violation of this chapter is a class A violation under
title 1, chapter 9, article A, "General Enforcement Provisions", of this code.
Each day such violation continues shall be considered a separate violation.
(Ord. 211, 8-5-2015)
3-15-4: CIVIL ACTION:
In addition to, or in lieu of, the imposition of a fine, Malheur County may
initiate a civil action against any person or entity violating this chapter for
any and all remedies available under Oregon law, including, but not limited to,
obtaining mandatory and prohibitory injunctions and orders of abatement.
Malheur County shall be entitled to collect its costs and expenses, including
reasonable attorney fees incurred at trial, hearing or on appeal. (Ord. 211, 8-
5-2015)
3-15-5: SEVERABILITY:
If any part or section of this chapter is invalid or unenforceable in any
respect for any reason, the validity and enforceability of any such provision
in any other respect and of the remaining provisions of this chapter shall not
be in any way impaired. (Ord. 211, 8-5-2015)
3-15-6: EMERGENCY CLAUSE:
The Malheur County court hereby adjudges that it is necessary for the immediate
preservation of the peace, health, and safety of the county that this chapter
shall take effect immediately upon its passage and approval, and an emergency
is hereby declared to exist and this chapter will be in full force and effect
immediately upon its passage by the Malheur County court. (Ord. 211, 8-5-2015)
CHAPTER 16
TRUANCY FROM MALHEUR COUNTY SCHOOLS
SECTION:
3-16-1:    Title
3-16-2: Authority And Purpose
3-16-3:    Jurisdiction
3-16-4:    Definitions
3-16-5:    Conduct Prohibited
3-16-6:    Proceedings
3-16-7:    Order To Attend School; Conditions; Fine To Responsible Adult; Refer
To District Attorney
3-16-8:    Separate Offense
3-16-1:   TITLE:
This chapter shall be known as "Truancy from Malheur County Schools". (Ord.
230, 4-5-2023)
3-16-2:   AUTHORITY AND PURPOSE:
   A.   The Malheur County Court has authority to regulate matters of County
concern within the County, under the provisions of the Constitution of the
State of Oregon and the revised statutes of the State of Oregon.
   B.   This chapter applies to students (Kindergarten (K) - 12th grades)
enrolled in a full-time public school located within Malheur County, including
within the incorporated cities of Nyssa, Ontario, Vale, Jordan Valley and
Adrian, the city councils of which have consented pursuant to ORS 203.040.
   C.   This chapter does not apply to students attending private schools
located within Malheur County, including within the incorporated city of
Ontario.
   D.   The purpose of this chapter is to create rules for enforcement
procedures intended to reduce the incidents of truancy within public schools in
Malheur County. It is in the best interest of a student to attend school
regularly and complete the educational courses of study. (Ord. 230, 4-5-2023)
3-16-3:   JURISDICTION:
The Malheur County Justice Court and Vale Municipal/Justice Court have
jurisdiction and venue over infractions and proceedings of this chapter. Venue
for truancy occurs at the school district office where the student is enrolled.
(Ord. 230, 4-5-2023)
3-16-4:   DEFINITIONS:
 
                                   A Student is not attending School for ten
CHRONIC ABSENTEEISM:               percent (10%) or more of School days in a
                                   School year.
                                   Malheur County Sheriff Deputy, city police
LAW ENFORCEMENT OFFICIAL:          officer, or Malheur County Juvenile
                                   Department Counselor.
                                   A full-time school operated by Adrian
                                   School District No.61, Annex Charter
                                   School District No. 29, Arock School
PUBLIC SCHOOL IN MALHEUR COUNTY OR District No. 81, Four Rivers Charter
SCHOOL:                            School, Harper Charter School No. 66,
                                   Jordan Valley School District No. 3,
                                   Juntura School District, Nyssa School
                                   District No. 26, Ontario School District
                                   No. 8C and Vale School District No. 84.
                                   A person at least eighteen (18) years of
RESPONSIBLE ADULT:                 age, who is the parent, guardian or
                                   otherwise authorized to have the care or
                                   custody of a Student.
                                   Any personnel appointed/designated by a
                                   School or the Education Service District
SCHOOL OFFICIAL:                   Region 84 in Malheur County including but
                                   not limited to principal, vice-principal,
                                   superintendent, resource officer, or
                                   truancy enforcement specialist.
                                   A minor between the ages of five through
                                   eighteen (5-18) who has not completed the
STUDENT:                           twelfth (12th) grade and is enrolled in a
                                   Public School in Malheur County. (Ord.
                                   230, 4-5-2023)
 
3-16-5:   CONDUCT PROHIBITED:
   A.   Except as otherwise provided herein, students are required to attend
school and shall not be chronically absent. For the purpose of this section
"chronically absent" means to miss ten percent (10%) or more of school days in
a school year. It is unlawful for a student to have chronic absenteeism from
school as required by this chapter.
   B.   Every responsible adult having the custody or care of a student shall
make every reasonable effort to prevent the student from violating this
chapter, and shall supervise the student by sending the student to school and
maintaining the student in school so that the student does not miss ten percent
(10%) or more of school days.
   C.   This chapter does not limit or supersede any provision of Oregon law,
which exempts certain children from compulsory school attendance (ORS 339.030),
nor does this ordinance limit the duties, powers and responsibilities of public
school officials. (Ord. 230, 4-5-2023)
3-16-6:   PROCEEDINGS:
   A.   A law enforcement official or school official may issue a citation to a
student and responsible adult for violating this chapter as set out in section
3-16-5  above.
   B.   Prior to issuing a citation, the Superintendent of Education Service
District Region 84 or school district superintendent shall provide the student
and responsible adult with written notification to include the following
content:
      1.   The student is required to attend school, and the student is deemed
chronically absent in violation of this chapter and state rule.
      2.   The failure of a responsible adult to send the student to school and
maintain the student in school so that the student does not miss ten percent
(10%) or more of school days is a violation of this chapter.
      3.   The student and responsible adult may be cited to Justice Court for
chronic absenteeism under this chapter.
      4.   The student and responsible adult must attend a conference with a
designated school official on a specified date and time where expectations for
the student's regular attendance at school will be outlined.
      5.   The student and responsible adult have the right to request an
evaluation if the student is not on an individualized education program (IEP).
If the student is on an IEP, the right to request a review of the IEP.
   C.   Following the notification and process in subsection B above, if the
Student remains chronically absent from School in violation this chapter or the
Student or Responsible Adult fails to attend the conference in subsection B.
4., an infraction citation will be issued. The citation shall be substantially
in the form as set out in Malheur County Code
1-9A-4-4 . The citation will direct the Student (if the Student is in the 6th
through 12th grade) and the Responsible Adult to appear at Justice Court on a
designated date and time.
   D.   If a Responsible Adult fails to appear at the date and time issued on
the citation, the Justice of the Peace shall continue the matter and issue an
order/show cause for the Responsible Adult to appear. A warrant will be issued
for the Responsible Adult who fails to appear at such show cause proceeding.
(Ord. 230, 4-5-2023)
3-16-7:   ORDER TO ATTEND SCHOOL; CONDITIONS; FINE TO RESPONSIBLE ADULT; REFER
TO DISTRICT ATTORNEY:
   A.   Order To Attend School. Upon finding a violation of this chapter, the
Justice of the Peace shall enter an order requiring the student to attend
school and not miss ten percent (10%) or more of school days; and order the
responsible adult to send the student to school and maintain the student in
school so that the student does not miss ten percent (10%) or more of school
days.
   B.   Conditions Imposed to Suspend Imposition of Fine, Dismiss Violation and
Discharge Responsible Adult. In addition to the Order in subsection
3-16-6 , A. if the responsible adult seeks suspension of the fine in subsection
3-16-6 , C. dismissal and discharge of the violation under this chapter, the
Justice of Peace shall impose conditions with which the student and/or
responsible adult must meet. Conditions imposed by the Justice of the Peace
shall include, but are not be limited, to:
      1.   Review. Set future dates and time for the student and responsible
adult to personally appear and provide progress reports demonstrating the
student's proof of attendance, grades, and other school-related information
determined by the Justice of the Peace.
      2.   Require student and/or responsible adult to complete and engage in
recommendations of an age-appropriate and relevant class, group or program in
person or on-line, such as, but not limited to: Needs Assessment by local
mental authority; a parent mentor or parent effectiveness program, support
group that promotes parenting, mental, behavioral, or emotional wellness,
truancy intervention classes, or academic classes for the Student after school
or on the weekend. Costs, if any, will be paid by a responsible adult.
   C.   Fine. A violation of this chapter is a Class A civil infraction under
the Malheur County Code subject to a fine imposed on the responsible adult of
up to five hundred dollars ($500) for the first offense; and up to one thousand
dollars ($1,000) each subsequent offense. The fine shall be suspended, the
civil infraction dismissed and the responsible adult discharged if the Order in
subsection
3-16-6 , A. and the conditions in subsection
3-16-6 , B. are met to the satisfaction of the court. If the responsible adult
fails to comply with the Order in subsection
3-16-6 , A. and the conditions in subsection
3-16-6 , B., the court shall impose the fine authorized by this chapter.
   D.   There may only be one suspension of the fine under this subsection with
respect to a responsible adult.
   E.   The Justice of the Peace, School Official or a Law Enforcement Official
shall, when the circumstances are appropriate, refer responsible adults to the
District Attorney's Office for prosecution in Malheur County Circuit Court/
Juvenile Court under ORS 163.577 (1) (c). (Ord. 230, 4-5-2023)
3-16-8: SEPARATE OFFENSE:
Each violation of this chapter shall be a separate offense. (Ord. 230, 4-5-
2023)
CHAPTER 17
USE OF COUNTY PROPERTY FOR CAMPING
SECTION:
3-17-1:    Purpose And Scope
3-17-2:    Definitions
3-17-3:    Time, Place And Manner Regulations
3-17-4:    Vehicles, Automobiles Or Recreational Vehicles
3-17-5:    Violations And Enforcement
3-17-1:   PURPOSE AND SCOPE:
   A.   Purpose. The purpose of this chapter is to adequately protect the
health, safety and public welfare of the County by addressing time, place and
manner camping regulations that identify when, where, and how camping is
allowed on County property, as well as define enforcement and compliance. This
chapter addresses camping in tents and other portable shelters.
   B.   Scope. This chapter is meant to regulate the use of County property and
is not intended to regulate activities on private property or property owned by
other public entities. This chapter does not allow violation of other
ordinances, rules or laws of the County or within the city limits of Nyssa,
Ontario, Vale, Adrian or Jordan Valley. (Ord. 232, 6-21-2024)
3-17-2:   DEFINITIONS:
For purposes of this chapter, the following terms and phrases have the meanings
assigned to them below:
 
                    Include, but are not limited to, tents, huts, temporary
CAMP FACILITIES:    shelters, lean-tos, or any other temporary and removal
                    structures or parts thereof.
                    To pitch, erect, create, use, or occupy camp facilities for
CAMP OR CAMPING:    the purposes of habitation, as evidenced by the use of camp
                    paraphernalia.
                    Includes, but is not limited to, tarpaulins, cots, beds,
                    sleeping bags, blankets, mattresses, hammocks, or outdoor
CAMP PARAPHERNALIA: cooking devices and similar equipment.
                    Note. Camp facilities and camp paraphernalia do not include
                    vehicles, automobiles or recreation vehicles used for
                    camping.
 
 
                      Any locations where one or more persons have temporary
CAMPSITE:             sleeping or living accommodations by use of camp
                      facilities and/or camp paraphernalia.
                      All real property, land, and right-of-way owned, leased
COUNTY PROPERTY:      (either to County or by County), controlled, or managed
                      by the County.
ESTABLISHED CAMPSITE: A campsite in place for over twenty-four (24) consecutive
                      hours in one location.
                      An item that can reasonably be identified as belonging to
PERSONAL PROPERTY:    an individual and that has apparent value or utility.
                      Personal property includes camp facilities and camp
                      paraphernalia.
RECREATIONAL FIRE:    A fire for the cooking of food, warmth, fellowship or
                      ceremonial purposes.
                      Roads, and other public right-of-way dedicated and
                      accepted by the County, either in fee title or as holder
                      of a public easement for right-of-way or public access
                      purposes. Public rights-of-way include but are not
RIGHT-OF-WAY:         limited to any County Road, local access road or other
                      property that is subject to a public access easement
                      dedicated or granted to the County for vehicular,
                      pedestrian or other means. This includes roads maintained
                      and within a rural road assessment district.
                      Public or private elementary, middle or high school or
SCHOOL:               other school attended primarily by children under
                      eighteen (18) years of age. (Ord. 232, 6-21-2024)
 
3-17-3:   TIME, PLACE AND MANNER REGULATIONS:
Camping is permitted on County property subject to the time, place, and manner
regulations contained herein.
   A.   Time Regulations. Except as expressly authorized in the Malheur County
Code, County's camping policy, rules adopted for a County park or by the County
Court, camping is prohibited on any County property between the hours of seven
o’clock to ten o’clock (7:00 a.m. to 10:00 p.m.).
   B.   Place Regulations. Except as expressly authorized in the Malheur County
Code, or by the Malheur County Court, it shall be unlawful for any person to
camp on the following County property:
      1.   Cow Hollow Park without permission from the park manager, County or
Cow Hollow Park Association.
      2.   Bully Creek Park without the permission of the park manager. Bully
Creek Park is the boundary of the recreation area managed by the County under a
Management Agreement with Bureau of Reclamation.
      3.   Arcadia Industrial Park Subdivision.
      4.   Malheur County Courthouse and all surrounding parking lots used for
Courthouse parking.
      5.   On or within any County road right-of-way, including undeveloped
right-of-ways.
      6.   On or within any County property zoned Ontario - College District
(O-CD) (such as Extension Office property.
      7.   Any County property that is fenced, posted with signs such as "keep
out" or "no trespassing" or otherwise not open to the public.
      8.   Within five hundred (500) feet of any public, private or parochial
school and childcare facility or preschool as defined in ORS 329A.250 as
amended.
      9.   Within twenty-five (25) feet of the public entrance to a business,
including the front entrance of a County business.
      10.   Within twenty-five (25) feet of a public or private driveway.
      11.   On or within one hundred (100) feet of County property located
within any area zoned residential or industrial on the County or city zoning
maps or ordinances in effect at the time.
      12.   All County Property along Lytle Boulevard leased to private
individuals for grazing.
      13.   Malheur County Fairgrounds and parking lots used for the
fairgrounds.
      14.   Malheur County Community Correction developed lot and paved parking
area.
      15.   Stone House Museum.
      16.   Brogan Community Park.
      17.   Malheur County Health Department.
      18.   Malheur County Justice Court.
      19.   Any property not within three (3) miles of a city's limits (In
other words more than three (3) miles from the city limits of Vale, Ontario,
Nyssa, Adrian and Jordan Valley).
      20.   Any County property designated as no camping at any time by County
Court resolution, including without limitation, modification or amendment to
places designated or not designated in this Section 16-3-3 B.
   C.   Manner Regulations. At times and locations where camping is permitted
under this chapter, the following regulations apply:
      1.   Camping in a manner that reduces the clear, continuous sidewalk
width to less than three (3) feet is prohibited. Camping that obstructs fire
hydrants or clear vision for traffic, pedestrians or traffic devices is
prohibited.
      2.   At no time may huts, lean-tos, shacks, or any other structures,
whether constructed with plywood, wood materials, pallets, or other materials,
be built, or placed on County property for camping. Items such as tents and
similar items used for shelter that are readily portable are not prohibited by
this section.
      3.   Camping must be limited within a spatial footprint of one hundred
fifty (150) square feet in surface area. The intent of this section is to allow
a person to sleep and maintain essentials, while still maintaining the ability
of everyone to use public spaces as designed and intended. A group of up to
three (3) may camp together (group camps). To prevent larger campsites and the
cumulative impacts that can result, group camps may not be within one hundred
fifty (150) feet of any group camps.
      4.   Individuals may not accumulate, discard or leave behind garbage,
debris, unsanitary or hazardous materials, or other items of no apparent
utility on County property, or on any adjacent public or private property.
      5.   Open flames, recreational fires, burning of garbage, bonfires, or
other fires, flames, or heating deemed unsafe by the County environmental
health director, applicable fire district or applicable city fire department
are prohibited. Some cooking stoves and other means of keeping warm may be
permitted.
      6.   Dumping of gray water (i.e., waste water from baths, sinks, and the
like) or black water (i.e., sewage) into any facilities or places not intended
for gray water or black water disposal is prohibited. This includes but is not
limited to storm drains, which are not intended for disposal of gray water or
black water.
      7.   Digging, excavation, terracing of soil, alteration of property or
infrastructure, or damage to vegetation or trees is prohibited. Unauthorized
connections to utilities and use of power generators are prohibited.
      8.   Storage of personal property such as tires, gasoline, lumber,
furniture, extra propane tanks, combustible material, lumber or other items or
materials (except as needed for an individual to camp, sleep or keep warm and
dry) is prohibited.
      9.   Except as expressly authorized by the Malheur County Code, all
persons are prohibited from leaving personal property, camp facilities and camp
paraphernalia, unattended on any County property for more than twenty-four (24)
hours.
      10.   All animals on County property must be leashed or crated at all
times. (Ord. 232, 6-21-2024)
3-17-4:   VEHICLES, AUTOMOBILES OR RECREATIONAL VEHICLES:
It is prohibited at all times for any person to use County property to camp in
vehicles, automobiles or recreation vehicles, provided the County Court may, in
its discretion, designate certain County properties or portions of properties
where camping in licensed and fully operable vehicles, automobiles or
recreation vehicles may be allowed on a limited basis, and may set the terms
and conditions of camping that may be allowed. Any such use of County property
will follow environmental health and building code provisions. (Ord. 232, 6-21-
2024)
3-17-5:   VIOLATIONS AND ENFORCEMENT:
   A.   Violation. A violation of this chapter is a Class D civil infraction.
Citations will only be issued when other means of achieving compliance have
been unsuccessful or are not practical for the situation. Violators will be
cited into the Malheur County Justice Court.
   B.   Prior to civil infraction. Before a civil infraction citation is
issued, the County enforcement officer will contact the person(s) and provide a
reasonable opportunity to cure or remedy the alleged violation. The enforcement
officer shall consider weather conditions, if the person has a disability and
other appropriate factors in determining a reasonable period of time to cure.
In most cases, the enforcement officer will assess whether the person subject
to the citation has been referred to service providers, and make a referral if
it appears none have been made.
   C.   Campsite and Property Removal. A violation of this chapter may result
in the removal of an established campsite (existing more than twenty-four (24)
hours). In addition, when enforcement personnel determine a campsite endangers
public health and safety, the campsite may be removed immediately.
   Typically, removal of a campsite and clean-up of the camp, camp material,
camp paraphernalia or other personal property will not occur until after a
request for voluntary compliance has been made, except in the case of an
exceptional emergency, such as possible contamination by hazardous materials, a
public health emergency or when there is an immediate danger to human life or
safety or illegal activities. Any camp, camp materials, camp paraphernalia or
personal property in violation of the standards or manner regulations in this
chapter may be removed or cleaned-up by the County or its contractors, subject
to the requirements in section D below. A campsite and individul may be subject
to removal or citation, or both.
   D.   Policies Related to Campsite and Personal Property Removal.
      1.   Prior to removing an established campsite on County property, at
least seventy-two (72) hours in advance, except in the case of emergency,
danger to human life or safety or criminal/illegal activity, the County will
post notice (in English and Spanish) at the location of the established
campsite stating the individuals must leave and all remaining personal property
will be removed by the County. The notice will state: (a) an address where the
unclaimed personal property will be stored; (b) list a phone number and hours a
person can claim ownership and collect or make arrangements to collect their
personal property; or (c) list a phone number and address individuals may call
to find out where the property will be stored. The County will also inform
local agencies that deliver services to homeless individuals that such notice
has been posted and the location of the notice.
      2.   A campsite may be removed for violation of this chapter without
posting a seventy-two (72) hour notice when there are grounds for law
enforcement officials to believe that illegal activity, other than camping, is
occurring on the campsite or in the immediate vicinity of the campsite, or the
property that comprises the campsite is being used or intended to be used to
commit or facilitate the commission of otherwise illegal activity; or in the
event of an exceptional emergency, such as possible site contamination by
hazardous materials or when there is a an immediate danger to human life or
safety.
      3.   Once the seventy-two (72) hour notice has been posted, the County
may remove the established campsite and personal property beginning seventy-
two (72) hours after posting and for up to ten (10) days following the posting.
      4.   After the established campsite has been removed subject to a
seventy-two (72) hour notice or for campsites when no advance notice is
required due to the circumstances, the camp and all associated camp facilities,
camp paraphernalia and personal property can be removed by County.
      5.   When removing individuals and property from campsites, enforcement
personnel will make reasonable efforts to remove individuals without the use of
force, arrest or citation.
      6.   When removing camp facilities, camp paraphernalia and personal
property, the County will make reasonable efforts to determine if the property
belongs to an individual and if it has any apparent value or utility. The
County will make reasonable efforts to identify which established campsite
personal property was removed from and aid in connecting people with their
property. Items that are perishable, or have no apparent use or value, or that
are in an unsanitary condition due to saturation or contamination from bodily
fluids, whether human or animal, or other contamination, will be considered
garbage, discarded and not stored.
      7.   Weapons, drug paraphernalia, or other contraband, and items that
appear to be either stolen or evidence of a crime shall be given to law
enforcement officials. Items that appear ro have a value of one thousand
dollars ($1,000) or more shall be given to law enforcement officials for
storage and safe keeping, and shall be made available as described in section
D9 below.
      8.   When personal property, camp paraphernalia and camp facilities are
removed and notice was not provided in D1 the County must post notice at or
near as possible to the location where the personal property was collected. The
notice will state where the personal property is being stored, list a phone
number and hours a person can claim ownership and collect or make arrangements
to collect their personal property.
      9.   Personal property removed from a campsite and unclaimed at the time
of removal will be stored by the County for a minimum of thirty (30) days, or
the duration required by law at the time of the removal. To the extent
possible, the County will store personal property at a County building or
facilities in the same community of the campsite so that individuals can
reasonably retrieve personal property. The County will make reasonable efforts
to provide a range of times the storage location will be available for
individuals to collect their personal property. The County may dispose of any
personal property that remains unclaimed after thirty (30) days, or such
duration as required by law. (Ord. 232, 6-21-2024)
TITLE 4
PROPERTY AND FACILITY REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
COUNTY PARKS
SECTION:
4-1-1:   Regulations And Restrictions; Scope
4-1-2:   Class A Infractions
4-1-3:   Class D Infractions
4-1-4:   Enforcement Officer
4-1-5:   Other Remedies
4-1-6:   Other Rules Of Park
4-1-1: REGULATIONS AND RESTRICTIONS; SCOPE:
The following regulations apply to use by the public of Bully Creek Park and
Reservoir, a County recreation facility. (Ord. 110, 4-29-1997)
4-1-2: CLASS A INFRACTIONS:
   A.   Vehicle Restrictions:
      1.   No person shall operate any motorized vehicle except upon designated
roadways and in the reservoir.
      2.   No person shall drive upon a roadway within Bully Creek Park in
excess of ten (10) miles per hour.
      3.   No person shall park a motor vehicle, boat, trailer on the grass or
other marked areas prohibiting the parking of vehicles.
   B.   Discharge Of Firearms/Possession Of Loaded Firearms: No person shall
discharge a firearm, pellet gun, blow gun, crossbow, bow and arrow, or any
weapon which acts by force of explosion. No person shall possess a loaded
firearm. This subsection does not apply or affect:
      1.   A person discharging a firearm in the lawful defense of person or
property;
      2.   A law enforcement officer in the performance of official duty; and
      3.   A member of the military in the performance of official duty.
   C.   Sale And Use Of Fireworks: No person shall sell or use fireworks. For
purposes of this subsection, "fireworks" includes unclassified items exempt
from the definition of "fireworks" in the Oregon Fireworks Law including
sparklers, snakes, and smoke producing items.
   D.   Swimming And Boating: No person shall swim or water-ski from the boat
moorage docks or in the area of the boat launch ramp and dock bounded by the
shoreline, marked buoys parallel to the shoreline, by the swimming area and by
marker buoys perpendicular to the shoreline.
   E.   Deposit Of Trash: No person shall discard any glass, cans or other
trash, rubbish, debris, refuse or litter on land or water, other than in
receptacles provided for the purpose of holding such trash, rubbish, debris or
litter. There shall be no dumping of human waste or gray water tanks in the
restroom sinks, toilets, urinals or fish cleaning facility. A dumping station
for such items is available at the park entrance.
   F.   Park Hours: No person shall enter or remain in park area between posted
closing and opening time, except where overnight camping is permitted.
   G.   Nonseason Use Prohibited: No person shall enter the park when the park
is closed to the public from November 15 to April 15 of each year; and at such
times as may be determined by the County Court, considering the weather
conditions and other factors which may constitute a threat to the health,
safety and welfare of the public.
   H.   Burning And Fires: It is a violation of this Chapter for any person to
build a fire outside designated areas for fires, outside of a stove, fireplace,
grill or fire ring; to leave a fire unattended; to fail to extinguish a fire
before leaving the park area and failure to obey posted restrictions on fires
during high fire hazard conditions.
   I.   Removal Of Trees, Shrubs, Flowers And Other Foliage: Except with
permission from the park manager, no person shall sever, cut down, mutilate or
remove any tree, timber, shrub or flowers from Bully Creek Park.
   J.   Continuous Overnight Camping: No person shall continuously camp at
Bully Creek Park without the permission of the park manager. No individual may
designate Bully Creek Park as an address or receive mail at the park without
the permission of the park manager. (Ord. 110, 4-29-1997; amd. Ord. 232, 6-21-
2023)
4-1-3: CLASS D INFRACTIONS:
   A.   Animal Restrictions:
      1.   No person shall bring, keep, maintain or allow livestock, including
cattle, horses, pigs, sheep or goats.
      2.   No owner or person in control shall allow a dog to run at large.
Dogs shall be on a leash.
   B.   Metal Detectors: No person shall use a metal detector without the park
manager's permission.
   C.   Signs And Concessions:
      1.   It is a violation of this Chapter for any person to operate a
concession, fixed or mobile; or solicit, sell or offer for sale any goods,
wares, foods, liquids or services without the park manager's written permission
and, if applicable, without a license from the Malheur County Environmental
Health Officer.
   D.   Camping By Homeless Individuals. It shall be unlawful to camp, as
defined in Malheur County Code Title 3 Chapter 17, at Bully Creek Park without
the permission of the park manager. (Ord. 110, 4-29-1997; amd. Ord. 232, 6-21-
2023)
4-1-4: ENFORCEMENT OFFICER:
The person(s) who may issue infraction citations for violating this Chapter are
the caretaker of the Bully Creek Park and any "enforcement officer" defined in
Section
1-9A-1 of this Code. (Ord. 110, 4-29-1997)
4-1-5: OTHER REMEDIES:
The rights and remedies provided above are not exclusive and are in addition to
any other rights and remedies provided by law. Individuals who violate this
Chapter may be liable to Malheur County in a civil action for any and all
damages done to property in Bully Creek Park. (Ord. 110, 4-29-1997)
4-1-6: OTHER RULES OF PARK:
The public shall comply with other rules developed by the park manager which
are posted within Bully Creek Park and amended from time to time. Noncompliance
with such rules can result in violation of this Chapter, State law, removal
from the park and any and all other action provided by law. (Ord. 110, 4-29-
1997; amd. Ord. 232, 6-21-2023)
ARTICLE A. COW HOLLOW PARK
SECTION:
4-1A-1: Regulations And Restrictions; Scope
4-1A-2: Infractions
4-1A-3: Enforcement Officer
4-1A-4: Other Remedies
4-1A-5: Other Rules Of Park
4-1A-1: REGULATIONS AND RESTRICTIONS; SCOPE:
The following regulations apply to use by the public of Cow Hollow Park (park),
a county recreation facility. The national park service, U.S. department of
interior donated Cow Hollow Park to Malheur County for public recreational uses
through the federal lands to parks program. (Ord. 188, 11-3-2010)
4-1A-2: INFRACTIONS:
   A.   The following are class A infractions:
      1.   Vehicle Restrictions:
         a.   No person shall operate any motorized vehicle except upon
designated roadways.
         b.   No person shall drive upon a roadway in Cow Hollow Park in excess
of ten (10) miles per hour.
         c.   No person shall park a motor vehicle or trailer on the grass,
unless in a designated overnight or day use area.
      2.   Discharge Of Firearms: No person shall discharge a firearm, pellet
gun, blowgun or any other weapon that acts by force or explosion. This
subsection does not apply to a person discharging a firearm in the lawful
defense of person or property or to a law enforcement officer in the
performance of official duty.
      3.   Sale And Use Of Fireworks: No person shall sell or use fireworks.
      4.   Deposit Of Trash: No person shall discard any glass, cans or other
trash, rubbish, debris, refuse or litter on land, other than in receptacles
provided for the purpose of holding such trash, rubbish, debris or litter.
There shall be no dumping of human waste or gray water tanks in the restroom
sinks, toilets or urinals. There are no RV dumping facilities at the park.
      5.   Park Hours: Day use is from dawn to dusk.
      6.   Use Prohibited: Absent written permission, no person shall use the
park when the park is closed to the public at such times as may be determined
by the county court considering the weather conditions and other factors which
may constitute a threat to the health, safety and welfare of the public.
      7.   Burning And Fires: It is a violation for any person to build a fire
outside designated areas for fires, outside of a stove, fireplace, grill or
fire ring; to leave a fire unattended; to fail to extinguish a fire before
leaving the park area and failure to obey posted restrictions on fires during
high fire hazard conditions.
      8.   Removal Of Trees, Shrubs, Flowers And Other Foliage: No person shall
sever, cut down, mutilate or remove any tree, timber, shrub or flower from Cow
Hollow Park.
      9.   Continuous Overnight Camping: No person shall continuously camp at
Cow Hollow Park for longer than fourteen (14) days without the permission of
the county.
      10.   Damage: No person shall destroy, deface, damage, impair or remove
any part of the park or improvements on the park.
   B.   The following are class D infractions:
      1.   Animal Restrictions:
         a.   No person shall bring, keep, maintain or allow livestock of
cattle, pigs, sheep or goats.
         b.   No owner or person in control shall allow a dog to run at large.
      2.   Signs And Concessions: It is a violation for any person to operate a
concession, fixed or mobile; or solicit, sell or offer for sale any goods,
wares, foods, liquids or services without the county's permission and, if
applicable, without a license from the Malheur County environmental health
officer.
      3.   Camping By Homeless Individuals. It shall be unlawful to camp, as
defined in Malheur County Code
Title 3 Chapter 17 , at Cow Hollow Park without the permission of the county,
Cow Hollow Park Association, or the park manager. (Ord. 188, 11-3-2010; amd.
Ord. 232, 6-21-2023)
4-1A-3: ENFORCEMENT OFFICER:
The person(s) who may issue infraction citations for violating these rules and
regulations is any "enforcement officer" defined in section
1-9A-2 of this code. (Ord. 188, 11-3-2010)
4-1A-4: OTHER REMEDIES:
The rights and remedies provided above are not exclusive and are in addition to
any other rights and remedies provided by law. Individuals who violate this
chapter may be liable to Malheur County in a civil action for any and all
damages done to property in Cow Hollow Park. (Ord. 188, 11-3-2010)
4-1A-5: OTHER RULES OF PARK:
The public shall comply with other rules developed for the park, which are
posted within the park and amended from time to time. (Ord. 188, 11-3-2010)
CHAPTER 2
RURAL MAPS AND ADDRESSES
SECTION:
4-2-1:   Rural Maps And Addresses Adopted
4-2-2:   Planning Director's Responsibility
4-2-3:   Amendment And Update To Maps
4-2-4:   Posting Of Addresses
4-2-5:   Authorized Designee
4-2-1: RURAL MAPS AND ADDRESSES ADOPTED:
   A.   The Malheur County rural maps and addresses (hereinafter referred to as
"maps"), as presented to the county court, are hereby accepted and adopted as
the official county diagrammatic layout of roads and streets within the
unincorporated areas of Malheur County, for the purpose and for use as the
official means of assigning and locating addresses within the county.
   B.   The names of roads and streets as set forth on said maps are adopted as
the official Malheur County road and street names.
   C.   The addresses set forth on said maps are adopted as set forth thereon
and shall henceforth be used as official county addresses. The planning
director or authorized designee shall be responsible for assigning all future
addresses, making corrections and adjustments in the addressing maps and
notifying the affected property owners, post office and utility companies.
   D.   The Malheur County rural maps and addresses, as compiled, are hereby
incorporated herein by reference and adopted as if set forth in full. A true
and correct copy of said maps with corrections and adjustments shall be on file
with the county planning department. It is understood that these maps will be
updated by the planning department as needed and as provided herein.
   E.   Copies of the official Malheur County rural maps and addresses shall be
available for sale to the public at a cost established by approved motion of
the county court. (Ord., 4-7-1987)
4-2-2: PLANNING DIRECTOR'S RESPONSIBILITY:
It shall be the responsibility of the planning director to issue proper
addresses to each new residential and legitimate business structure for which
approval is granted for a zoning permit. Each new residential and business
structure shall be numbered in the manner set forth in section 4-2-4 of this
chapter. At the discretion of the planning director and upon application, an
unoccupied structure or facility may be assigned an address if it is necessary
to identify the site for assessment, utility connections, insurance, emergency
services or other similar reasons. Home occupations and vacant property will
not be issued addresses. (Ord. 153, 5-18-2005)
4-2-3: AMENDMENT AND UPDATE TO MAPS:
The county court shall cause said maps, as officially accepted and adopted
herein, to be updated at least annually. Such updates shall be available to the
public at a cost established by approved motion of the county court. (Ord., 4-
7-1987)
4-2-4: POSTING OF ADDRESSES:
All existing structures for which an address is set forth on said maps shall be
renumbered with the address set forth on the appropriate map, said numerals to
be at least two and one- half inches (21/2") in height, placed at a driveway
opening or on a building so as to be clearly visible from the center of the
road or street facing said structure. All individuals affected hereby shall
number their mailboxes in accordance with U.S. postal regulations. Failure to
comply with the provisions of this section constitutes a violation of county
ordinance 1 . (Ord., 4-7-1987)
 
Notes
1 1. See subsection
  1-9A-3C of this code.
4-2-5: AUTHORIZED DESIGNEE:
Pursuant to subsection
4-2-1C of this chapter, the Malheur County planning director may, within his
discretion and upon approval of the Malheur County court by motion and minutes,
designate any city planning director and/or city staff member within an
incorporated city of Malheur County to be the authorized designee to assign
future addresses, make corrections and adjustments to in the addressing maps
and notify the affected property owners, post office and utility companies
within that city's urban growth area. (Ord. 109, 1-21-1997, eff. 1-21-1997)
CHAPTER 3
ESTABLISHMENT OF PROVISIONS FOR CREATION AND ADMINISTRATION OF REIMBURSEMENT
DISTRICTS
   SECTION:
4-3-1:   Purpose
4-3-2:   Definitions
4-3-3:   Application To Establish A Reimbursement District
4-3-4:   Public Works Director's Report
4-3-5:   Amount To Be Reimbursed
4-3-6:   Public Hearing
4-3-7:   County Court Action
4-3-8:   Notice Of Adoption Of Resolution
4-3-9:   Recording The Resolution
4-3-10:   Contesting The Reimbursement District
4-3-11:   Obligation To Pay Reimbursement Fee
4-3-12:   Public Improvement(s)
4-3-13:   Multiple Public Improvements
4-3-14:   Collection And Payment; Other Fees And Charges
4-3-15:   Nature Of The Reimbursement Fee
4-3-16:   Administration
4-3-1: PURPOSE:
   A.   The purpose of a reimbursement district is to provide local government
and developers a method for sharing all or a portion of the costs of
constructing public improvements with benefited properties which have the
opportunity to use the public improvement. A reimbursement district is an
alternative procedure to formation of a local improvement district.
   B.   Owners of property which would be subject to a reimbursement fee will
be provided an opportunity to review and comment on pertinent information prior
to the county establishing a district pursuant to this chapter. The county will
collect the reimbursement fee and, upon receipt will forward the funds to the
person who constructed the public improvement.
   C.   A developer may include a city, special district, road assessment
district or private person or entity.
   D.   The reimbursement fees established under this chapter are intended to
become due and payable upon development of benefited property. Such charges are
fees for service because they contemplate a development's receipt of essential
infrastructure and services based upon the nature of development. The timing
and extent of any development are within the control of the developer. The
reimbursement fee imposed under this chapter is not intended to be a tax on
property or on a property owner as a direct consequence of ownership of
property within the meaning of section 11b of article XI of the Oregon
constitution of the legislation implementing that section.
   E.   The county requires developers to construct certain public improvements
necessary to serve proposed developments. Often these public improvements,
particularly those constructed off site, can and will benefit other property
owners when they develop their property. Therefore, these improvements
represent a benefit to those property owners.
   F.   The development of public improvements in order to enable new
development, particularly in the urban growth area, is a county goal. The
management of the urban growth area is shared jointly between the county and
the applicable city within Malheur County. City water, sanitary sewer, storm
sewer and street improvements are necessary to serve proposed developments in
the urban growth areas. These public improvements are constructed in accordance
with city and county design and construction standards and later dedicated as
"public improvements". (Ord. 155, 4-5-2006)
4-3-2: DEFINITIONS:
The following terms are defined as follows for the purposes of this chapter:
   COUNTY: The county of Malheur, Oregon.
   DEVELOPER: The county, city, special district or a person who is required or
chooses to finance some or all of the cost of a street, water or sewer
improvement which is available to provide service to property, other than
property owned by the person, and who applies to the county for reimbursement
for the expense of the public improvement.
   DEVELOPMENT PERMIT: Any final land use decision, limited land use decision,
partition, subdivision, excavation, conditional use, temporary use or right of
way access permit.
   PERSON: A natural person, the person's heirs, executors, administrators or
assigns; a firm, partnership, corporation, association, legal entity, city,
special district, road assessment district, or the county, its or their
successors or assigns; and any agent, employee or representative thereof.
   PUBLIC IMPROVEMENT: Any construction, reconstruction or upgrading of water,
storm water, sewer or road improvements. Road improvement includes, but is not
limited to, road, curbs, sidewalks, gutters, storm drains and public rights of
way.
   PUBLIC WORKS DIRECTOR: The public works director of Malheur County.
   REIMBURSEMENT AGREEMENT: The agreement between the developer and the county
which is authorized by the county court, providing for the installation of and
payment for public improvements within the reimbursement district.
   REIMBURSEMENT DISTRICT: The area which is determined by the county court to
derive a benefit from the construction of public improvements, financed in
whole or in part by the developer.
   REIMBURSEMENT FEE: The fee required to be paid by a resolution of the county
court and, if the developer is not the county, the reimbursement agreement. The
county court resolution and reimbursement agreement shall determine the
boundaries of the reimbursement district and shall determine the methodology
for imposing a fee which considers the cost of reimbursing the developer for
financing the construction of the public improvement within the reimbursement
district. (Ord. 155, 4-5-2006)
4-3-3: APPLICATION TO ESTABLISH A REIMBURSEMENT DISTRICT:
   A.   A person who is required to or chooses to finance some or all of the
cost of public improvement(s) which will be available to provide service to
property other than property owned by the person may by written application
filed with the public works director request that the county establish a
reimbursement district. The public improvement(s) must be of a size greater
than that which would otherwise ordinarily be required in connection with an
application for a building permit or development permit or must be available to
provide service to property other than property owned by the developer, so that
the public will benefit by making the public improvement(s).
   B.   The application shall be accompanied by an application fee, in an
amount established by county resolution, which the county court has determined
reasonable to cover the cost of the preparation of the public works director's
report and notice pursuant to this chapter.
   C.   The application shall include the following:
      1.   A written description of the location, type, size and cost of each
public improvement which is to be eligible for reimbursement.
      2.   A map showing the boundaries of the proposed reimbursement district,
the tax account number of each property, its size and boundaries.
      3.   A map showing the properties to be included in the proposed
reimbursement district; the zone for the properties; the front footage and
square footage of said properties, or similar data necessary for calculating
the apportionment of the cost of the public improvement(s); the property or
properties owned by the developer; and the names and mailing addresses of
owners of other properties to be included in the proposed reimbursement
district.
      4.   The actual or estimated cost of the public improvement(s). (Ord.
155, 4-5-2006)
4-3-4: PUBLIC WORKS DIRECTOR'S REPORT:
The public works director shall review the application for the establishment of
a reimbursement district and evaluate whether a reimbursement district should
be established. The public works director may require the submission of other
relevant information from the developer in order to assist in the evaluation.
The public works director shall prepare a written report for the county court
that considers and makes recommendation concerning each of the following
factors:
   A.   Whether the developer will finance, or has financed some or all of the
cost of the public improvement(s), thereby making service available to property
other than that owned by the developer.
   B.   The boundary and size of the proposed reimbursement district.
   C.   The actual or estimated cost of the public improvement(s) serving the
area of the proposed reimbursement district and the portion of the cost for
which the developer should be reimbursed for each public improvement.
   D.   A methodology for spreading the cost among the properties within the
reimbursement district and, where appropriate, defining a "unit" for applying
the reimbursement fee to property which may, with county approval, be
partitioned, subdivided, developed, altered or modified at some future date.
   E.   The amount to be charged by the county for an administration fee for
the reimbursement agreement. The administration fee shall be fixed by the
county court and shall be included in the resolution approving and forming the
reimbursement district. The administration fee is due and payable to the county
at the time the reimbursement agreement is signed.
   F.   Whether the public improvement(s) shall or have met the county
standards.
   G.   Whether it is fair and in the public interest to create a reimbursement
district. (Ord. 155, 4-5-2006)
4-3-5: AMOUNT TO BE REIMBURSED:
   A.   A reimbursement fee shall be computed by the county for all properties
within the reimbursement district, excluding property owned by or dedicated to
a city, the county or the state of Oregon, which have the opportunity to use
the public improvements, including the property of the developer. The
reimbursement fee shall be calculated separately for each public improvement.
The developer shall not be reimbursed for the portion of the reimbursement fee
computed for the developer's own property.
   B.   The cost to be reimbursed to the developer shall be limited to the cost
of construction engineering, construction, and off site dedication and/or
acquisition of right of way property. Construction engineering shall include
surveying and inspection costs and shall not exceed seven and one-half percent
(7.5%) of eligible public improvement construction costs. Costs to be
reimbursed for right of way property shall be limited to the reasonable market
value of land or easements purchased by the developer from a third party in
order to complete the public improvement(s).
   C.   No reimbursement shall be allowed for the cost of design engineering,
financing costs, permits or fees required for construction permits, land or
easements dedicated by the developer, the portion of costs which are eligible
for systems development charge credits or any costs which cannot be clearly
documented.
   D.   Reimbursement for legal expenses shall be allowed only to the extent
that such expenses relate to the preparation and filing of an application for
reimbursement, and, in the case of the county or city acting as developer, the
attorney fees and costs related to any condemnation proceeding involving
property within the reimbursement district.
   E.   Reimbursement for the amount of the application fee required by
subsection
4-3-3B of this chapter. (Ord. 155, 4-5-2006)
4-3-6: PUBLIC HEARING:
   A.   Within forty five (45) days after the public works director has
completed the report required in section
4-3-4 of this chapter, the county court shall hold an informational public
hearing in which any person shall be given the opportunity to comment on the
proposed reimbursement district. Because formation of the reimbursement
district does not result in an assessment against property or lien against
property, the public hearing is for informational purposes only and is not
subject to mandatory termination because of remonstrances. The county court has
the sole discretion after the public hearing to decide whether a resolution
approving and forming the reimbursement district shall be adopted.
   B.   Not less than ten (10) days prior to any public hearing held pursuant
to this chapter, the developer and all owners of property within the proposed
reimbursement district shall be notified of the public hearing and the purpose
thereof. Such notification shall be accomplished by regular and certified mail
or by personal service. Notice shall be deemed effective on the date that the
letter of notification is mailed. Failure of the developer or any affected
property owner to be notified shall not invalidate or otherwise affect any
reimbursement district resolution or the county court's action to approve the
same.
   C.   If a reimbursement district is formed prior to construction of the
public improvement(s), a second public hearing, subject to the same notice
requirements, shall be held after the public improvement has been accepted by
the county. At that time, the county, at its discretion, may modify the
resolution to reflect the actual cost of the public improvement(s). (Ord. 155,
4-5-2006)
4-3-7: COUNTY COURT ACTION:
   A.   After the public hearing held pursuant to subsection
4-3-6A of this chapter, the county court shall approve, reject or modify the
recommendations contained in the public works director's report. The county
court's decision shall be contained in a resolution. If a reimbursement
district is established, the resolution shall include the public works
director's report as approved or modified, and specify that payment of the
reimbursement fee, as designated for each property within the reimbursement
district, is a precondition of receiving any county permits applicable to
development of that parcel as further provided in section
4-3-11 of this chapter.
   B.   The resolution shall establish an interest rate to be applied to the
reimbursement fee as a return on the investment of the developer. The interest
rate shall be fixed and computed against the reimbursement fee as simple
interest and shall not compound.
   C.   The resolution shall instruct the county to enter into an agreement
with the developer pertaining to the public improvement(s) within the
reimbursement district. If the reimbursement agreement is entered into prior to
construction, the reimbursement agreement shall be contingent upon the public
improvement(s) being accepted by the county. The reimbursement agreement shall
contain at least the following provisions:
      1.   The public improvement(s) shall meet all applicable county
standards.
      2.   The total amount of potential reimbursement to the developer shall
be specified.
      3.   The total amount of potential reimbursement shall not exceed the
actual cost of the public improvement(s).
      4.   The developer shall guaranty the public improvement(s) for a period
of twelve (12) months after the date of installation.
      5.   A clause in a form acceptable to county counsel stating that the
developer shall defend, indemnify and hold harmless the county from any and all
losses, claims, damage, judgments or other costs or expense arising as a result
of or related to the county's establishment of the reimbursement district,
including any county costs, expenses and attorney fees related to collection of
the reimbursement fee should the county court decide to pursue collection of an
unpaid reimbursement fee under subsection
4-3-11I of this chapter.
      6.   A clause in a form acceptable to county counsel stating that the
developer agrees that the county cannot be held liable for any of the
developer's alleged damages, including all costs and attorney fees, under the
reimbursement agreement or as a result of any aspect of the formation of the
reimbursement district, or the reimbursement district process, and that the
developer waives, and is stopped from bringing, any claim of any kind,
including a claim in inverse condemnation, because the developer has benefited
by the county's approval of its development and the required public improvement
(s).
      7.   Other provisions the county determines necessary and proper to carry
out the provisions of this chapter.
   D.   If a reimbursement district is established by the county court, the
date of the formation of the reimbursement district shall be the date that the
county court adopts the resolution forming the reimbursement district. (Ord.
155, 4-5-2006)
4-3-8: NOTICE OF ADOPTION OF RESOLUTION:
The county shall notify all property owners within the reimbursement district
and the developer of the adoption of a reimbursement district resolution. The
notice shall include a copy of the resolution, the date it was adopted and a
short explanation specifying the amount of the reimbursement fee and that the
property owner is legally obligated to pay the reimbursement fee pursuant to
this chapter. (Ord. 155, 4-5-2006)
4-3-9: RECORDING THE RESOLUTION:
Notice of the formation and nature of the reimbursement district will be
recorded in the office of the Malheur County clerk so as to provide notice to
potential purchasers of property within the reimbursement district. Said
recording shall not create a lien. Failure to make such recording shall not
affect the legality of the resolution or the obligation to pay the
reimbursement fee. (Ord. 155, 4-5-2006)
4-3-10: CONTESTING THE REIMBURSEMENT DISTRICT:
No legal action intended to contest the formation of the reimbursement district
or the reimbursement fee, including the amount of the reimbursement fee
designated for each property within the reimbursement district, shall be filed
after sixty (60) days following the adoption of a resolution establishing a
reimbursement district and any such legal action shall be exclusively by writ
of review pursuant to ORS 34.010 to 34.102. (Ord. 155, 4-5-2006)
4-3-11: OBLIGATION TO PAY REIMBURSEMENT FEE:
   A.   The applicant for a permit related to property within any reimbursement
district shall pay the county, in addition to any other applicable fees and
charges, the reimbursement fee established by the county court if, within
twenty five (25) years after the date of the passage of the resolution forming
the reimbursement district, the person applies for and receives approval from
the county for any of the following activities:
      1.   A building permit for a new building or structure.
      2.   A building permit(s) for any addition(s), modification(s), repair(s)
or alteration(s) of a building, which exceed twenty five percent (25%) of the
value of the building within any twelve (12) month period. The value of the
building shall be the amount shown on the most current records of the Malheur
County assessor's office for the building's real market value. This subsection
A2 shall not apply to repairs made necessary due to damage or destruction by
fire or other natural disaster.
      3.   A "development permit", as that term is defined by this chapter.
      4.   Connection to or use of the public improvement(s).
   B.   The county's determination of who shall pay the reimbursement fee and
when the reimbursement fee is due is final.
   C.   In no instance shall the county, or any officer or employee of the
county, be liable for payment of any reimbursement fee, or portion thereof, as
a result of the county's determination as to who should pay the reimbursement
fee. Only those payments which the county has received from or on behalf of
those properties within a reimbursement district shall be payable to the
developer. The county's general fund or other revenue sources shall not be
liable for or subject to payment of outstanding and unpaid reimbursement fees
imposed upon private property.
   D.   Nothing in this chapter is intended to modify or limit the authority of
the county to provide or require access management.
   E.   Nothing in this chapter is intended to modify or limit the authority of
the county to enforce development conditions which have already been imposed
against specific properties.
   F.   Nothing in this chapter is intended to modify or limit the authority of
the county, in the future, to impose development conditions against specific
properties as the properties develop.
   G.   No person shall be required to pay the reimbursement fee on an
application or upon property for which the reimbursement fee has been
previously paid, unless such payment was for a different type of improvement.
No permit shall be issued for any of the activities listed in subsection A of
this section unless the reimbursement fee, together with the amount of accrued
interest, has been paid in full. Where approval is given as specified in
subsection A of this section, but no permit is requested or issued, then the
requirement to pay the reimbursement fee lapses if the underlying approval
lapses.
   H.   The reimbursement fee is immediately due and payable to the county by
property owners upon use of the public improvement(s) as provided in subsection
A of this section. If connection is made or construction commenced without
required county permits, then the reimbursement fee is immediately due and
payable upon the earliest date that any such permit was obtained.
   I.   Whenever the full reimbursement fee has not been paid and collected for
any reason after it is due, the county administrative officer shall report to
the county court the amount of the uncollected reimbursement, the legal
description of the property on which the reimbursement fee is due, the date
upon which the reimbursement fee was due and the property owner's name or
names. The county court shall then, by motion, set a public hearing date and
direct the county administrative officer to give notice of that hearing to each
of the identified property owners, together with a copy of the county
administrative officer's report concerning the unpaid reimbursement fee. Such
notice may be accomplished by regular and certified mail or personal service.
At the public hearing, the county court may accept, reject or modify the county
administrative officer's report. If the county court determines that the
reimbursement fee is due but has not been paid for whatever reason, the county
court may, at its sole discretion, act, by resolution, to take any action it
deems appropriate, including all legal or equitable means necessary, to collect
the unpaid reimbursement fee amount. After the county court has made the
determination that the reimbursement fee is due but has not been paid, the
developer shall have a private cause of action against the person legally
responsible for paying the reimbursement fee. (Ord. 155, 4-5-2006)
4-3-12: PUBLIC IMPROVEMENT(S):
Public improvements installed pursuant to reimbursement agreements shall become
and remain the sole property of the county or applicable city if in the urban
growth boundary. (Ord. 155, 4-5-2006)
4-3-13: MULTIPLE PUBLIC IMPROVEMENTS:
More than one public improvement may be the subject of a reimbursement
district. (Ord. 155, 4-5-2006)
4-3-14: COLLECTION AND PAYMENT; OTHER FEES AND CHARGES:
   A.   The developer shall receive all reimbursements collected by the county
for public improvements within the reimbursement district. Such reimbursements
shall be delivered to the developer for as long as the reimbursement agreement
is in effect. Such payments shall be made by the county within ninety (90) days
of receipt of the reimbursements.
   B.   The reimbursement fee is not intended to replace or limit, and is in
addition to, any other existing fees or charges collected by the county. (Ord.
155, 4-5-2006)
4-3-15: NATURE OF THE REIMBURSEMENT FEE:
